<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">
<li value="1"><a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> is the capital and <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> is the historic capital of Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li><li value="2">2014 estimate. A new estimate has been added in order to give a more correct GDP per capita.</li><li value="3">Preliminary results of 2011 census, which excluded four northern Serb-majority municipalities where it could not be carried out.</li><li value="4">Adopted unilaterally; Kosovo is not a formal member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>.</li><li value="5">Assigned 15 December 2016 to Kosovo by ITU.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%2B381" class="mw-redirect" title="+381">+381</a> was previously used for fixed lines. Kosovo-licensed mobile-phone providers used <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Monaco" title="Telephone numbers in Monaco">+377</a> (Monaco) or <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Slovenia" title="Telephone numbers in Slovenia">+386</a> (Slovenia) instead.</li><li value="6">XK is a "user assigned" ISO 3166 code not designated by the standard, but used by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbank" title="Deutsche Bundesbank">Deutsche Bundesbank</a> and other organisations. However, <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:RS" title="ISO 3166-2:RS">ISO 3166-2:RS</a> remains in use.</li>
</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kosovo</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Kosova</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔva]</a></span> or <i lang="sq" title="Albanian language text">Kosovë</i>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr-Cyrl">Косово</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[kôsoʋo]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Kosovo</b> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">Republika e Kosovës</i>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">Република Косово</span> / <i>Republika Kosovo</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">partially recognised</a> <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_disputes" title="List of territorial disputes">disputed territory</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a> that <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">declared independence</a> from <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> in February 2008. Covering an area of 10,908 square kilometres (4,212&#160;sq&#160;mi), Kosovo is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> territory in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> to the west and the uncontested territory of Serbia to the north and east. Due to its strategic position in the Balkan Peninsula, it serves as an important link in the connection between <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, while other major urban areas include <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pe%C4%87" title="Peć">Peć</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferizaj" title="Ferizaj">Ferizaj</a>. While Serbia recognises administration of the territory by Kosovo's elected government,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> it continues to claim it as its own <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kosovo" title="History of Kosovo">history</a> of Kosovo dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> era, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">Vinča</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo</a> cultures. During the <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Classical</a> period, it was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrian</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dardanians_(Balkans)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dardanians (Balkans)">Dardanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_settlement_of_Eastern_Europe" title="Celtic settlement of Eastern Europe">Celtic</a> people. In 168 BC, the area was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, it was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empires</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a> of 1389 is considered to be one of the defining moments in <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Serbia">Serbian medieval history</a>. The region was the core of the Serbian medieval state, which has also been the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> from the 14th century, when its status was upgraded to a patriarchate.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kosovo was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> from the 15th to the early 20th century. In the late 19th century, it became the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_National_Awakening" title="Albanian National Awakening">Albanian National Awakening</a>. Following their defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a>, the Ottomans <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1913)" title="Treaty of London (1913)">ceded</a> Kosovo to Serbia and Montenegro. Both countries joined <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and following a period of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavism" title="Yugoslavism">Yugoslav unitarianism</a> in the Kingdom, the post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> constitution established the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a> within the Yugoslav constituent Republic of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Republic of Serbia">Serbia</a>. Tensions between Kosovo's Albanian and Serb communities simmered through the 20th century and occasionally erupted into major violence, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> of 1998 and 1999, which resulted in the withdrawal of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of Serbia and Montenegro">Yugoslav Army</a> and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo</a>.
</p><p>On 17 February 2008, Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared its independence</a> from Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> It has since gained <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113&#160;UN member states</a>. Serbia <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_je_Srbija" title="Kosovo je Srbija">refuses to recognize</a> Kosovo as a state,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> although with the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement of 2013</a>, it has accepted the legitimacy of its institutions. Kosovo has a lower-middle-income economy and has <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Kosovo" title="International rankings of Kosovo">experienced</a> solid economic growth over the last decade by international financial institutions, and has experienced growth every year since the onset of the <a href="/wiki/2008_global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 global financial crisis">2008 global financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional_Cooperation_Council" title="Regional Cooperation Council">Regional Cooperation Council</a> and has applied for membership in the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_the_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation</a> as an observer and <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Kosovo" title="Names of Kosovo">Names of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png/220px-Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png/330px-Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png/440px-Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png 2x" data-file-width="1113" data-file-height="845" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_balkans_4thcentury.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a> in the 4th century during the sovereignty of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The entire region that today corresponds to the territory is commonly referred to in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> simply as <i>Kosovo</i> and in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> as <i>Kosova</i> or <i>Kosovë</i> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_grammar" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian grammar">definite form</a>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔːva]</a></span>) or <i><i lang="sq" title="Albanian language text">Kosovë</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_grammar" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian grammar">"indefinite" form</a>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian" title="Help:IPA/Albanian">[kɔˈsɔːv]</a></span>). In Serbia, a formal distinction is made between the eastern and western areas; the term <i><i lang="sr-Latn" title="Serbian language text">Kosovo</i></i> (<span lang="sr" title="Serbian language text">Косово</span>) is used for the eastern part centred on the historical <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo field (region)">Kosovo Field</a>, while the western part is called <i><a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a></i> (<span lang="sr" title="Serbian language text">Метохија</span>) (known as <i>Dukagjini</i> in Albanian).<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-serbia_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-serbia-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to one theory, <i>Kosovo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr-Cyrl">Косово</span>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[kôsoʋo]</a></span>) is the Serbian neuter <a href="/wiki/Possessive_adjective" class="mw-redirect" title="Possessive adjective">possessive adjective</a> of <i>kos</i> (кос) "<a href="/wiki/Turdus_merula" class="mw-redirect" title="Turdus merula">blackbird</a>", an <a href="/wiki/Ellipsis_(linguistics)" title="Ellipsis (linguistics)">ellipsis</a> for <i>Kosovo Polje</i>, 'blackbird field', the name of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_field_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo field (region)">a plain</a> situated in the eastern half of today's Kosovo and the site of the 1389 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Inc.2015_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inc.2015-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The name of the plain was applied to <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">the Kosovo Province</a> created in 1864.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> also refer to Kosovo as <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>, the name of a Roman province formed in 165 BC, which covered the territory of modern Kosovo. The name is derived from ancient tribe of <a href="/wiki/Dardani" title="Dardani">Dardani</a>, ultimately from proto-Albanian word <i>dardha/dardā</i> which means "pear".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The former Kosovo President <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Rugova" title="Ibrahim Rugova">Ibrahim Rugova</a> had been an enthusiastic backer of a "Dardanian" identity and the Kosovan flag and presidential seal refer to this national identity. However, the name "Kosova" remains more widely used among the Albanian population.
</p><p>The current borders of Kosovo were drawn while part of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">SFR Yugoslavia</a> in 1945, when the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija_(1945%E2%80%931963)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Region of Kosovo and Metohija (1945–1963)">Autonomous Region of Kosovo and Metohija (1945–1963)</a> was created as an administrative division of the new <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of Serbia">People's Republic of Serbia</a>. In 1963, it was raised from the level of an autonomous region to the level of an autonomous province as the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija_(1963%E2%80%931968)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija (1963–1968)">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija (1963–1968)</a>. In 1968, the dual name "Kosovo and <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a>" was reduced to a simple "Kosovo" in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo</a>. In 1990, the province was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The official conventional long name of the state is <i>Republic of Kosovo</i>, as defined by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution of Kosovo</a>, and is used to represent Kosovo internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, as a result of an <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">arrangement agreed between Pristina and Belgrade</a> in talks mediated by the European Union, Kosovo has participated in some international forums and organisations under the title "Kosovo*" with a footnote stating "This designation is without prejudice to positions on status, and is in line with UNSC 1244 and the ICJ Opinion on the Kosovo declaration of independence". This arrangement, which has been dubbed the "asterisk agreement", was agreed in an 11-point arrangement agreed on 24 February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kosovo" title="Geography of Kosovo">Geography of Kosovo</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/12px-Commons-logo.svg.png" width="12" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/18px-Commons-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/24px-Commons-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1376" /> See also: <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_Kosovo" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of Kosovo">Atlas of Kosovo</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Commons" title="Wikimedia Commons">Wikimedia Commons</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paradise_Lost.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/220px-Paradise_Lost.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/330px-Paradise_Lost.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Paradise_Lost.jpg/440px-Paradise_Lost.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paradise_Lost.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical landscape in <a href="/wiki/Rugova_(region)" title="Rugova (region)">Rugova</a> within <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Bjeshkët e Nemuna</a></div></div></div>
<p>A landlocked region, Kosovo occupies the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>. It has a total area of 10,908 square kilometres (4,212 square miles). It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42°</a> and <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">20°</a> and <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_east" title="22nd meridian east">22° E</a>. Kosovo is encircled by <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the south and southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the north, northeast and east.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kosovo's northernmost point is Bellobërda at 43° 14' 06" northern latitude; the southernmost is Restelica at 41° 56' 40" northern latitude; the westernmost point is <a href="/wiki/Bog%C3%AB,_Kosovo" title="Bogë, Kosovo">Bogë</a> at 20° 3' 23" eastern longitude; and the easternmost point is <a href="/wiki/Desivojca" title="Desivojca">Desivojca</a> at 21° 44' 21" eastern longitude. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/%C4%90eravica" title="Đeravica">Gjeravica</a> at 2,656 metres (8,714&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>, and the lowest is the <a href="/wiki/White_Drin" title="White Drin">White Drin</a> at 297 metres (974&#160;ft).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brod_Dragash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/220px-Brod_Dragash.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/330px-Brod_Dragash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Brod_Dragash.jpg/440px-Brod_Dragash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2394" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brod_Dragash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a> encompass one-tenth of Kosovo's territory.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Most of the Kosovo's borders are dominated by mountainous or high terrain. The most noticeable <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topographical</a> features are the <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Bjeshkët e Nemuna</a> and the <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ar_Mountains" title="Šar Mountains">Šar Mountains</a>. The Bjeshkët e Nemuna, also known as the Albanian Alps or Prokletije, are a geological continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a>. The mountains run laterally through the west along the border with Albania and Montenegro. The southeast is predominantly the Šar Mountains, which form the border with the Republic of Macedonia. Besides the mountain ranges, Kosovo's territory consists mostly of two major plains: the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Plain">Kosovo Plain</a> in the east and the <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija Plain</a> in the west.
</p><p>
Kosovo's hydrological resources are relatively small. The longest rivers of Kosovo include the <a href="/wiki/White_Drin" title="White Drin">White Drin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Morava" title="South Morava">South Morava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ibar_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibar River">Ibar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sitnica" title="Sitnica">Sitnica</a>, a tributary of Ibar, is the largest river lying completely within Kosovo's territory. River <a href="/wiki/Nerodimka_(river)" title="Nerodimka (river)">Nerodimka</a> represents Europe's only instance of a river bifurcation flowing into the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>.</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Kosovo" title="Biodiversity of Kosovo">Biodiversity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of Kosovo">Protected areas of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_,_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_,_Rugove.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/220px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/330px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg/440px-Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_%2C_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_%2C_Rugove.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4914" data-file-height="3255" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parku_Komb%C3%ABtar_Bjeshk%C3%ABt_Nemuna_,_Liqeni_i_madh_ne_Liqenat_,_Rugove.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna_National_Park" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park">Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park</a> is home to a wide range of flora and fauna species.</div></div></div>
<p>Located strategically in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>, Kosovo receives species from Europe and Eurasia. Forests are widespread in Kosovo and cover at least 39% of the country. <a href="/wiki/Phytogeographically" class="mw-redirect" title="Phytogeographically">Phytogeographically</a>, it straddles the <a href="/wiki/Illyria" title="Illyria">Illyrian</a> province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. In addition, it falls within the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mixed_forests" title="Balkan mixed forests">Balkan mixed forests</a> terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Palearctic_ecozone" class="mw-redirect" title="Palearctic ecozone">Palearctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest">Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-for_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-for-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo's biodiversity is conserved in two <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>, eleven <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> and one hundred three other protected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Both the <a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna_National_Park" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park">Bjeshkët e Nemuna National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharr_Mountains_National_Park" title="Sharr Mountains National Park">Sharr Mountains National Park</a> are the most important regions of vegeation and biodiversity inside Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Maxhuni_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maxhuni-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> encompasses more than 1,800 species of <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species, but the actual number is estimated to be higher than 2,500 species.<sup id="cite_ref-KOSOVObio_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KOSOVObio-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The diversity is the result of the complex interaction of geology and hydrology creating a wide variety of habitat conditions for flora growth. Although, Kosovo represents only 2.3% of the entire surface area of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, in terms of vegetation it has 25% of the Balkan flora and about 18% of the European flora.<sup id="cite_ref-KOSOVObio_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KOSOVObio-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The fauna is composed of a wide range of species.<sup id="cite_ref-Maxhuni_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maxhuni-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>14</span></sup> The mountainous west and southeast provide a great habitat for several <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> species including <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lynx" title="Lynx">lynxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_cat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild cat">wild cats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolve" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolve">wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_goat" title="Wild goat">wild goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roebucks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> A total of 255 species of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> have been recorded, with raptors such as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">eastern imperial eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_kestrel" title="Lesser kestrel">lesser kestrel</a> living principally in the mountains of Kosovo.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Kosovo" title="Climate of Kosovo">Climate of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/220px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/330px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg/440px-Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ost%C3%ABrvice_from_Brezovica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Snowy peak of <a href="/wiki/Pashallora" title="Pashallora">Pashallora</a> as seen from <a href="/wiki/Brezovica,_Kosovo" title="Brezovica, Kosovo">Brezovica</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Most of Kosovo experiences a <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> with <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The climate is strongly influenced by its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> in the west, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> in the south but also the European continental landmass in the north.
</p><p>The coldest areas of Kosovo are the mountains in the west and southeast, where an alpine climate is found. The warmest areas are mostly in the extreme southern areas close to the border with Albania, characterised by the Mediterranean climate. Mean monthly temperature ranges between 0&#160;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (32&#160;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) (in January) and 40&#160;°C (104&#160;°F) (in July). Mean annual precipitation ranges from 600 to 1,300&#160;mm (24 to 51&#160;in) per year, and is well distributed year-round.
</p><p>To the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Plain">Kosovo Plain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibar_(river)" title="Ibar (river)">Ibar Valley</a> are drier with total precipitation of about 600 millimetres (24 inches) per year and more influenced by continental air masses, with colder winters and very hot summers. In the southwest, climatic area of <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a> receives more mediterranean influences with warmer summers, somewhat higher precipitation (700&#160;mm (28&#160;in)) and heavy snowfalls in the winter. The mountainous areas of <a href="/wiki/Bjeshk%C3%ABt_e_Nemuna" class="mw-redirect" title="Bjeshkët e Nemuna">Bjeshkët e Nemuna</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/Shar_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Shar Mountains">Shar Mountains</a> on the south and <a href="/wiki/Kopaonik" title="Kopaonik">Kopaonik</a> in the north experiences alpine climate, with high precipitation (900 to 1,300&#160;mm (35 to 51&#160;in) per year, short and fresh summers, and cold winters.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The average annual temperature of Kosovo is 9.5&#160;°C (49.1&#160;°F). The warmest month is July with average temperature of 19.2&#160;°C (66.6&#160;°F), and the coldest is January with −1.3&#160;°C (29.7&#160;°F). Except <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istok" title="Istok">Istok</a>, all other meteorological stations in January recorded average temperatures under 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kosovo" title="History of Kosovo">History of Kosovo</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Archaeology_of_Kosovo" title="Archaeology of Kosovo">Archaeology of Kosovo</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goddness_of_Varos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Goddness_of_Varos.jpg/170px-Goddness_of_Varos.jpg" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Goddness_of_Varos.jpg/255px-Goddness_of_Varos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Goddness_of_Varos.jpg/340px-Goddness_of_Varos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1836" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Goddness_of_Varos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_in_Ferizaj" title="Culture in Ferizaj">Goddess of Varos</a> sun-baked ceramic figure dating back to the 6th millennium BC</div></div></div>
<p>In prehistory, the succeeding <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">Starčevo culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">Vinča culture</a> were active in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Authors_1975,_p.43_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Authors_1975,_p.43-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2017)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The area in and around Kosovo has been inhabited for nearly 10,000 years. During the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> age, Kosovo lay within the area of the <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da-Turda%C5%9F_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinča-Turdaş culture">Vinča-Turdaş culture</a> which is characterised by West Balkan black and grey pottery. <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_Europe" title="Bronze Age Europe">Bronze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age_Europe" title="Iron Age Europe">Iron Age</a> tombs have been found in <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jankovic_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jankovic-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The favorable position as well as abundant natural resources were ideal for the development of life since the prehistoric periods, proven by hundreds of archaeological sites discovered and identified throughout Kosovo, which proudly present its rich archeological heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-Milot_Berisha_2012,_Pg.7_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milot_Berisha_2012,_Pg.7-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The number of sites with archaeological potential is increasing, this as a result of findings and investigations that are carried out throughout Kosovo but also from many superficial traces which offer a new overview of antiquity of Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Milot_Berisha_2012,_Pg.7_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milot_Berisha_2012,_Pg.7-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/220px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/330px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hyjnesha_muze.jpg/440px-Hyjnesha_muze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyjnesha_muze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Goddess_on_the_Throne" title="Goddess on the Throne">Goddess on the Throne</a> is one of the most precious archaeological artifacts of Kosovo and has been adopted as the symbol of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>.</div></div></div><p>
The earliest traces documented in the territory of Kosovo belong to the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> Period, namely there are indications that cave dwellings might have existed like for example the Radivojce Cave set near the spring of the <a href="/wiki/Drin_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drin (river)">Drin</a> river, then there are some indications at Grnčar Cave in the <a href="/wiki/Vitina_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitina (town)">Vitina</a> municipality, Dema and Karamakaz Caves of <a href="/wiki/Pe%C4%87" title="Peć">Peć</a> and others. However, human settlement during the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> or Old Stone Age is not confirmed yet and not scientifically proven. Therefore, until arguments of Paleolithic and <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> man are confirmed, Neolithic man, respectively the Neolithic sites are considered as the chronological beginning of population in Kosovo.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/220px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/330px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg/440px-ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ULPIANA_foto_Arben_Llapashtica_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruins of Ancient <a href="/wiki/Ulpiana" title="Ulpiana">Ulpiana</a> situated south-east of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. The city played an important role in the development of one of the most important cities in the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Dardania_(Roman_province)" title="Dardania (Roman province)">Dardania</a>.</div></div></div><p> From this period until today Kosovo has been inhabited, and traces of activities of societies from prehistoric, ancient and up to medieval time are visible throughout its territory. Whereas, in some archaeological sites, multilayer settlements clearly reflect the continuity of life through centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During antiquity, the area which now makes up Kosovo was inhabited by various tribal ethnic groups, who were liable to move, enlarge, fuse and fissure with neighbouring groups. As such, it is difficult to locate any such group with precision. The <i>Dardani</i>, whose exact ethno-linguistic affiliation is difficult to determine, were a prominent group in the region during the late Hellenistic and early Roman eras.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The area was then conquered by Rome in the 160s BC, and incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Illyricum_(Roman_province)" title="Illyricum (Roman province)">Illyricum</a> in 59 BC. Subsequently, it became part of <a href="/wiki/Moesia_Superior" class="mw-redirect" title="Moesia Superior">Moesia Superior</a> in AD 87. The region was exposed to an increasing number of 'barbarian' raids from the 4th century AD onwards, culminating with the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_migrations" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic migrations">Slavic migrations</a> of the 6th and 7th centuries. Archaeologically, the early Middle Ages represent a hiatus in the material record,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurta2001189_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurta2001189-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and whatever was left of the native provincial population fused into the Slavs.<sup id="cite_ref-Stipčević1977_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stipčević1977-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ottoman_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Ottoman Kosovo">History of Ottoman Kosovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vilayet_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayet of Kosovo">Vilayet of Kosovo</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:113px;max-width:113px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:191px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10,_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_(1389).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png/111px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png" width="111" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png/167px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png/222px-Facial_Chronicle_-_b.10%2C_p.299_-_Battle_of_Kosovo_%281389%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1651" data-file-height="2860" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Russian miniature of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Kosovo Field">Battle of Kosovo</a> in 1389</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:115px;max-width:115px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:191px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Loza_nemanjica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Loza_nemanjica.jpg/113px-Loza_nemanjica.jpg" width="113" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Loza_nemanjica.jpg/170px-Loza_nemanjica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Loza_nemanjica.jpg/226px-Loza_nemanjica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="761" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A medieval fresco from the <a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Monastery of Decani</a> in 1335</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>The subsequent political and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Kosovo" title="Demographic history of Kosovo">demographic history of Kosovo</a> is not known with absolute certainty until the 13th century. Archaeological findings suggest that there was steady population recovery and progression of the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic culture">Slavic culture</a> seen elsewhere throughout the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>. The region was absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a> in the 850s, where <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine culture">Byzantine culture</a> was cemented in the region. It was re-taken by the Byzantines after 1018, and became part of the newly established Theme of Bulgaria. As the centre of Slavic resistance to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> in the region, the region often switched between Serbian and Bulgarian rule on one hand and Byzantine on the other, until Serbian Grand Prince <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Nemanja" title="Stefan Nemanja">Stefan Nemanja</a> secured it by the end of the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> An insight into the region is provided by the Byzantine historian-princess, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Comnena" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Comnena">Anna Comnena</a>, who wrote of "Serbs" being the "main" inhabitants of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest reference of the <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> comes from <a href="/wiki/Michael_Attaleiates" title="Michael Attaleiates">Michael Attaleiates</a>, who spoke of the <a href="/wiki/Arbanitai" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbanitai">Arbanitai</a> located around the hinterland districts of <a href="/wiki/Dyrrachium" class="mw-redirect" title="Dyrrachium">Dyrrachium</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Durrës</a>) on the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon2008_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon2008-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2014)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_Despotate_(1422)-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/170px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png" width="170" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/255px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg/340px-Serbian_Despotate_%281422%29-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="943" data-file-height="844" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbian_Despotate_(1422)-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bosnia" title="Kingdom of Bosnia">Kingdom of Bosnia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Despotate_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Despotate of Serbia">Despotate of Serbia</a> in 1422</div></div></div>
<p>The zenith of Serbian power was reached in 1346, with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>. During the 13th and 14th centuries, Kosovo became a political, cultural and religious centre of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Serbia (medieval)">Serbian Kingdom</a>. In the late 13th century, the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Archbishopric</a> was moved to <a href="/wiki/Pe%C4%87" title="Peć">Peć</a>, and rulers centred themselves between <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> during which time thousands of Christian monasteries and feudal-style forts and castles were erected.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Du%C5%A1an" title="Stefan Dušan">Stefan Dušan</a> used <a href="/wiki/Prizren_Fortress" title="Prizren Fortress">Prizren Fortress</a> as the capital of the Empire. When the Serbian Empire fragmented into a conglomeration of principalities in 1371, Kosovo became the hereditary land of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Brankovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Branković">House of Branković</a>. In the late 14th and the 15th centuries parts of Kosovo, the easternmost area of which was located near Pristina, were part of the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Dukagjini" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Dukagjini">Principality of Dukagjini</a>, which was later incorporated into an anti-Ottoman federation of all Albanian principalities, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Lezh%C3%AB" title="League of Lezhë">League of Lezhë</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sellers2010_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sellers2010-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Medieval_Monuments_in_Kosovo" title="Medieval Monuments in Kosovo">Medieval Monuments in Kosovo</a> is a today combined <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> consisting of four Serbian Orthodox churches and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Serbian_Orthodox_monasteries" title="List of Serbian Orthodox monasteries">monasteries</a>. The constructions were founded by members of <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a>, the most important dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1389 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Battle of Kosovo</a>, Ottoman forces defeated a coalition led by <a href="/wiki/Lazar_of_Serbia" title="Lazar of Serbia">Lazar Hrebeljanović</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jelavich1983_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jelavich1983-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prospect-magazine.co.uk_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prospect-magazine.co.uk-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Some historians, most notably <a href="/wiki/Noel_Malcolm" title="Noel Malcolm">Noel Malcolm</a> argues that the battle of Kosovo in 1389 did not end with an Ottoman victory and "Serbian statehood did survive for another seventy years."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, Lazar's son accepted Turkish nominal vassalage (as did some other Serbian principalities) and Lazar's daughter was married to the Sultan to seal the peace. By 1459, Ottomans conquered the new Serbian capital of Smederevo,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> leaving <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> under <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungarian</a> rule until second quarter of the 16th century.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="tsingle" data-file-height="2322" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Visoki Dečani Monastery</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:105px;max-width:105px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:68px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/103px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg" width="103" height="69" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/155px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/206px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87_(monastery)" title="Patriarchate of Peć (monastery)">Patriarchate of Peć</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Kosovo was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> from 1455 to 1912, at first as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of the Ottoman Empire">eyalet</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a>, and from 1864 as a separate <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">province</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Vilayet" title="Vilayet">vilayet</a></i>). During this time, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was introduced to the population. The <a href="/wiki/Vilayet_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayet of Kosovo">Vilayet of Kosovo</a> was an area much larger than today's Kosovo; it included all today's Kosovo territory, sections of the <a href="/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak" title="Sandžak">Sandžak</a> region cutting into present-day <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umadija_and_Western_Serbia" title="Šumadija and Western Serbia">Šumadija and Western Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> along with the <a href="/wiki/Kuk%C3%ABs" title="Kukës">Kukës</a> municipality, the surrounding region in present-day northern <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and also parts of north-western <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> with the city of <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a> (then Üsküp), as its capital. Between 1881 and 1912 (its final phase), it was internally expanded to include other regions of present-day <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, including larger urban settlements such as <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tip" title="Štip">Štip</a> (<i>İştip</i>), <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">Kumanovo</a> (<i>Kumanova</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Kratovo,_Macedonia" title="Kratovo, Macedonia">Kratovo</a> (<i>Kratova</i>). Serbs likely formed a majority of Kosovo from the 8th to the mid-19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Some scholars, such as the historian Fredrick F. Anscombe, believe that medieval and Ottoman Kosovo was ethnically heterogeneous, with Serbs and Albanians dominating at different times.<sup id="cite_ref-Anscombe_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anscombe-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/220px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/330px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg/440px-Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4528" data-file-height="3200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Qendra_historike_e_Prizrenitaa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The city of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> was the capital of the Serbian Empire and later cultural and intellectual centre of Kosovo during the Ottoman period in the Middle Ages.</div></div></div>
<p>Kosovo was part of the wider Ottoman region to be occupied by Austrian forces during the Great War of 1683–99,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> but the Ottomans re-established their rule of the region. Such acts of assistance by the Austrian Empire (then arch-rivals of the Ottoman Empire), or Russia, were always abortive or temporary at best.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 1690, the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Patriarch">Serbian Patriarch</a> <a href="/wiki/Arsenije_III_%C4%8Carnojevi%C4%87" title="Arsenije III Čarnojević">Arsenije III</a> led thousands people from Kosovo to the Christian north, in what came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Serb_Migration" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Serb Migration">Great Serb Migration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In 1766, the Ottomans abolished the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87" title="Serbian Patriarchate of Peć">Patriarchate of Peć</a> and fully imposed the <i><a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">jizya</a></i> on its non-Muslim population.
</p><p>Although initially stout opponents of the advancing Turks, Albanian chiefs ultimately came to accept the Ottomans as sovereigns. The resulting alliance facilitated the mass conversion of Albanians to Islam. Given that the Ottoman Empire's subjects were divided along religious (rather than ethnic) lines, Islamisation greatly elevated the status of Albanian chiefs. Prior to this, they were organised along simple tribal lines, living in the mountainous areas of modern Albania (from Kruje to the Sar range).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Soon, they expanded into a depopulated Kosovo,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> as well as northwestern Macedonia, although some might have been autochthonous to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac46_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac46-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> However, Banac favours the idea that the main settlers of the time were Vlachs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBanac42_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBanac42-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many Albanians gained prominent positions in the Ottoman government. "Albanians had little cause of unrest", according to author Dennis Hupchik. "If anything, they grew important in Ottoman internal affairs."<sup id="cite_ref-hupchik_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hupchik-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In the 19th century, there was an <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire">awakening</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism" title="Ethnic nationalism">ethnic nationalism</a> throughout the Balkans. The underlying ethnic tensions became part of a broader struggle of Christian Serbs against Muslim Albanians.<sup id="cite_ref-prospect-magazine.co.uk_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prospect-magazine.co.uk-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The ethnic <a href="/wiki/National_Renaissance_of_Albania" class="mw-redirect" title="National Renaissance of Albania">Albanian nationalism</a> movement was centred in Kosovo. In 1878 the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Prizren" title="League of Prizren">League of Prizren</a> (<i lang="sq" title="Albanian language text">Lidhja e Prizrenit</i>) was formed.
This was a political organisation that sought to unify all the Albanians of the Ottoman Empire in a common struggle for autonomy and greater cultural rights,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> although they generally desired the continuation of the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The League was dis-established in 1881 but enabled the awakening of a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">national identity</a> among Albanians.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Albanian ambitions competed with those of the Serbs. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> wished to incorporate this land that had formerly been within its empire.
</p><p>During and after the <a href="/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_(1876%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian–Ottoman War (1876–78)">Serbian–Ottoman War</a> of 1876–78, between 30,000 and 70,000 Muslims, mostly Albanians, were <a href="/wiki/The_Expulsion_of_Albanians_1877-1878" class="mw-redirect" title="The Expulsion of Albanians 1877-1878">expelled</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces_of_the_Principality_of_Serbia" title="Armed forces of the Principality of Serbia">Serb army</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Ni%C5%A1" title="Sanjak of Niš">Sanjak of Niš</a> and fled to the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet" title="Kosovo Vilayet">Kosovo Vilayet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Batakovic1992_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batakovic1992-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elsie2010_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie2010-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Turk">Young Turk</a> movement took control of the Ottoman Empire after a coup in 1912 which deposed Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid&#160;II</a>. The movement supported a centralised form of government and opposed any sort of autonomy desired by the various nationalities of the Ottoman Empire. An allegiance to <a href="/wiki/Ottomanism" title="Ottomanism">Ottomanism</a> was promoted instead.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> An Albanian uprising in 1912 exposed the empire's northern territories in Kosovo and <a href="/wiki/Novi_Pazar" title="Novi Pazar">Novi Pazar</a>, which led to an invasion by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Dynasty">The Ottomans</a> suffered a serious defeat at the hands of Albanians in 1912, culminating in the Ottoman loss of most of its Albanian-inhabited lands. The Albanians threatened to march all the way to <a href="/wiki/Salonika" class="mw-redirect" title="Salonika">Salonika</a> and reimpose Abdul Hamid.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbia1913.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/220px-Serbia1913.png" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/330px-Serbia1913.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Serbia1913.png/440px-Serbia1913.png 2x" data-file-width="663" data-file-height="912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serbia1913.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Division of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_vilayet" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo vilayet">Kosovo vilayet</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a> (<i>yellow</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a> (<i>green</i>)  following the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a>  1913. See also <a href="/wiki/Albania_during_the_Balkan_Wars" title="Albania during the Balkan Wars">Albania during the Balkan Wars</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A wave of Albanians in the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Military of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman army</a> ranks also deserted during this period, refusing to fight their own kin. In September 1912, a joint Balkan force made up of Serbian, Montenegrin, Bulgarian and Greek forces drove the Ottomans out of most of their European possessions. The rise of nationalism unfortunately hampered relations between Albanians and <a href="/wiki/Serbs_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbs in Kosovo">Serbs in Kosovo</a>, due to influence from Russians, Austrians and Ottomans.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> After the Ottomans' defeat in the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1913)" title="Treaty of London (1913)">1913 Treaty of London</a> was signed with <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Western Kosovo (Metohija)</a> ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a> and Eastern Kosovo ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Soon, there were concerted Serbian colonisation efforts in Kosovo during various periods between Serbia's 1912 takeover of the province and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&#160;II</a>. So the population of Serbs in Kosovo fell after World War&#160;II, but it had increased considerably before then.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An exodus of the local Albanian population occurred. Serbian authorities promoted creating new Serb settlements in Kosovo as well as the assimilation of Albanians into Serbian society.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel_2001_20_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel_2001_20-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Numerous colonist Serb families moved into Kosovo, equalising the demographic balance between Albanians and Serbs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/190px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" width="190" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/285px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg/380px-Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="1050" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Germans_in_Kosovska_Mitrovica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German soldiers <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_persecution_of_Serbs" class="mw-redirect" title="World War II persecution of Serbs">set fire to a Serbian village</a> near <a href="/wiki/Mitrovica,_Kosovo" title="Mitrovica, Kosovo">Mitrovica</a>, circa 1941.</div></div></div>
<p>In the winter of 1915–16, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Kosovo saw the retreat of the Serbian army as Kosovo was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria%E2%80%93Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Austria–Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>. In 1918, the Allied Powers pushed the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> out of Kosovo. After the end of World War I, the Kingdom of Serbia was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenians</a> on 1 December 1918.
</p><p>Kosovo was split into four counties, three being a part of Serbia (<a href="/wiki/Zve%C4%8Dan" title="Zvečan">Zvečan</a>, Kosovo and southern <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a>) and one of Montenegro (northern Metohija). However, the new administration system since 26 April 1922 split Kosovo among three districts (<a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblast</a>) of the Kingdom: Kosovo, Raška and Zeta. In 1929, the country was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a> and the territories of Kosovo were reorganised among the <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Banovina" title="Zeta Banovina">Banate of Zeta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Morava_Banovina" title="Morava Banovina">Banate of Morava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vardar_Banovina" title="Vardar Banovina">Banate of Vardar</a>. In order to change the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kosovo" title="Demographics of Kosovo">ethnic composition of Kosovo</a>, between 1912 and 1941 a <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation of Kosovo">large-scale Serbian re-colonisation of Kosovo</a> was undertaken by the Belgrade government. Meanwhile, Kosovar Albanians' right to receive education in their own language was denied alongside other non-Slavic or unrecognised Slavic nations of Yugoslavia, as the kingdom only recognised the Slavic Croat, Serb, and Slovene nations as constituent nations of Yugoslavia, while other Slavs had to identify as one of the three official Slavic nations while non-Slav nations were only deemed as minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel_2001_20_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel_2001_20-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Albanians and other <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> were forced to emigrate, mainly with the land reform which struck Albanian landowners in 1919, but also with direct violent measures.<sup id="cite_ref-daskalovski_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daskalovski-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-malcolm_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malcolm-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In 1935 and 1938 two agreements between the Kingdom of Yugoslavia and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> were signed on the expatriation of 240,000 Albanians to Turkey, which was not completed because of the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Axis_invasion_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis invasion of Yugoslavia">Axis invasion of Yugoslavia</a> in 1941, most of Kosovo was assigned to Italian-controlled Albania, with the rest being controlled by Germany and Bulgaria. A three-dimensional conflict ensued, involving inter-ethnic, ideological, and international affiliations, with the first being most important. Nonetheless, these conflicts were relatively low-level compared with other areas of Yugoslavia during the war years, with one Serb historian estimating that 3,000 Albanians and 4,000 Serbs and Montenegrins were killed, and two others estimating war dead at 12,000 Albanians and 10,000 Serbs and Montenegrins.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> An official investigation conducted by the Yugoslav government in 1964 recorded nearly 8,000 war-related fatalities in Kosovo between 1941 and 1945, 5,489 of whom were Serb and Montenegrin and 2,177 of whom were Albanian.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> It is not disputed that between 1941 and 1945 tens of thousands of Serbs, mostly recent colonists, fled from Kosovo. Estimates range from 30,000 to 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> There had been large-scale Albanian immigration from Albania to Kosovo which is by some scholars estimated in the range from 72,000<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamet2006141_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamet2006141-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> to 260,000 people (with a tendency to escalate, the last figure being in a petition of 1985). Some historians and contemporary references emphasize that a large-scale migration of Albanians from Albania to Kosovo is not recorded in Axis documents.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communist_Yugoslavia">Communist Yugoslavia</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo</a></div>
