<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/220px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/330px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg/440px-Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SFR_Yugoslav_Albanian_Minority.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The flag of the Albanian Minority of Kosovo in the Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fadil_Hoxha,_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/180px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" width="180" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/270px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg/360px-Fadil_Hoxha%2C_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1362" data-file-height="1802" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fadil_Hoxha,_commander_of_Kosovo_partisans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fadil_Hoxha" title="Fadil Hoxha">Fadil Hoxha</a>, the Vice-President of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, from 1978 to 1979</div></div></div>
<p>The province as in its outline today first took shape in 1945 as the <i>Autonomous Kosovo-Metohian Area</i>. Until World War II, the only entity bearing the name of Kosovo had been a political unit carved from the former <a href="/wiki/Vilayet" title="Vilayet">vilayet</a> which bore no special significance to its internal population. In the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> (which previously controlled the territory), it had been a vilayet with its borders having been revised on several occasions. When the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Province, Ottoman Empire">Ottoman province</a> had last existed, it included areas which were by now either ceded to <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, or found themselves within the newly created Yugoslav republics of <a href="/wiki/SR_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="SR Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, or <a href="/wiki/SR_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="SR Macedonia">Macedonia</a> (including its previous capital, <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>) with another part in the <a href="/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak" title="Sandžak">Sandžak</a> region of southwest Serbia.
</p><p>Tensions between ethnic Albanians and the Yugoslav government were significant, not only due to ethnic tensions but also due to political ideological concerns, especially regarding relations with neighbouring Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Harsh repressive measures were imposed on Kosovo Albanians due to suspicions that there were sympathisers of the <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinist</a> regime of <a href="/wiki/Enver_Hoxha" title="Enver Hoxha">Enver Hoxha</a> of Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In 1956, a show trial in Pristina was held in which multiple Albanian Communists of Kosovo were convicted of being infiltrators from Albania and were given long prison sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> High-ranking Serbian communist official <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Rankovi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Ranković">Aleksandar Ranković</a> sought to secure the position of the Serbs in Kosovo and gave them dominance in Kosovo's <a href="/wiki/Nomenklatura" title="Nomenklatura">nomenklatura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in Kosovo at this time was repressed and both Albanians and Muslim Slavs were encouraged to declare themselves to be Turkish and emigrate to Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> At the same time Serbs and Montenegrins dominated the government, security forces, and industrial employment in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Albanians resented these conditions and protested against them in the late 1960s, accusing the actions taken by authorities in Kosovo as being colonialist, as well as demanding that Kosovo be made a republic, or declaring support for Albania.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the ouster of Ranković in 1966, the agenda of pro-decentralisation reformers in Yugoslavia, especially from Slovenia and Croatia, succeeded in the late 1960s in attaining substantial decentralisation of powers, creating substantial autonomy in Kosovo and Vojvodina, and recognising a <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Muslim Yugoslav</a> nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> As a result of these reforms, there was a massive overhaul of Kosovo's nomenklatura and police, that shifted from being Serb-dominated to ethnic Albanian-dominated through firing Serbs in large scale.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Further concessions were made to the ethnic Albanians of Kosovo in response to unrest, including the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Universiteti_i_Prishtin%C3%ABs" title="Universiteti i Prishtinës">University of Pristina</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> institution.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Katherine_Bokovoy_1992._Pp._296-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> These changes created widespread fear among Serbs that they were being made <a href="/wiki/Second-class_citizen" title="Second-class citizen">second-class citizens</a> in Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> By the 1974 Constitution of Yugoslavia, Kosovo was granted major autonomy, allowing it to have its own administration, assembly, and judiciary; as well as having a membership in the collective presidency and the Yugoslav parliament, in which it held veto power.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/220px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/330px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg/440px-SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SocialistYugoslavia_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Republics and provinces of the SFR Yugoslavia</div></div></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the 1974 constitution, concerns over the rise of Albanian nationalism in Kosovo rose with the widespread celebrations in 1978 of the 100th anniversary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Prizren" title="League of Prizren">League of Prizren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35_96-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._35-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Albanians felt that their status as a "minority" in Yugoslavia had made them second-class citizens in comparison with the "nations" of Yugoslavia and demanded that Kosovo be a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent republic</a>, alongside the other republics of Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1981_protests_in_Kosovo" title="1981 protests in Kosovo">Protests by Albanians in 1981 over the status of Kosovo</a> resulted in Yugoslav territorial defence units being brought into Kosovo and a state of emergency being declared resulting in violence and the protests being crushed.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath of the 1981 protests, purges took place in the Communist Party, and rights that had been recently granted to Albanians were rescinded&#160;– including ending the provision of Albanian professors and Albanian language textbooks in the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo._2000._Pp._36-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to very high <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rates</a>, the proportion of Albanians increased from 75% to over 90%. In contrast, the number of Serbs barely increased, and in fact dropped from 15% to 8% of the total population, since many Serbs departed from Kosovo as a response to the tight economic climate and increased incidents with their Albanian neighbours. While there was tension, charges of "genocide" and planned harassment have been debunked as an excuse to revoke Kosovo's autonomy. For example, in 1986 the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> published an official claim that Kosovo Serbs were being subjected to an Albanian program of 'genocide'.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though they were disproved by police statistics,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> they received wide attention in the Serbian press and that led to further ethnic problems and eventual removal of Kosovo's status. Beginning in March 1981, Kosovar Albanian students of the University of Pristina organised protests seeking that Kosovo become a republic within Yugoslavia and demanding their human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt19810419_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt19810419-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The protests were brutally suppressed by the police and army, with many protesters arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-hdk_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdk-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> During the 1980s, ethnic tensions continued with frequent violent outbreaks against Yugoslav state authorities, resulting in a further increase in emigration of Kosovo Serbs and other ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters19860527_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters19860527-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-csm19860728_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm19860728-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The Yugoslav leadership tried to suppress protests of Kosovo Serbs seeking protection from ethnic discrimination and violence.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt19870627_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt19870627-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kosovo_War">Kosovo War</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_in_the_Kosovo_War" title="War crimes in the Kosovo War">War crimes in the Kosovo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosova_(1990%E2%80%932000)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Kosova (1990–2000)">Republic of Kosova (1990–2000)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg/180px-Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg/270px-Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg/360px-Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kompleksi_i_sht%C3%ABpive_t%C3%AB_familjes_Jashari_ne_Prekaz_10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Adem_Jashari" title="Adem Jashari">Adem Jashari</a>, one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Liberation_Army" title="Kosovo Liberation Army">Kosovo Liberation Army</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: UÇK)</small></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg/220px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg/330px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg/440px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2969" data-file-height="1857" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_990618-M-5696S-016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._marines" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. marines">U.S. Marines</a> set up a road block near the village of Koretin on 16 June 1999.</div></div></div>
<p>Inter-ethnic tensions continued to worsen in Kosovo throughout the 1980s. In 1989, Serbian President <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>, employing a mix of intimidation and political manoeuvring, drastically reduced Kosovo's special autonomous status within Serbia and started cultural oppression of the ethnic Albanian population.<sup id="cite_ref-rogel_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogel-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo Albanians responded with a <a href="/wiki/Non-violent_resistance" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violent resistance">non-violent</a> separatist movement, employing widespread <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a> and creation of parallel structures in <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">education, medical</a> care, and taxation, with the ultimate goal of achieving the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence of Kosovo">independence of Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 1990, the Kosovo Albanians proclaimed the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosova_(1990%E2%80%932000)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Kosova (1990–2000)">Republic of Kosova</a>, and declared it a sovereign and independent state in September 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In May 1992, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Rugova" title="Ibrahim Rugova">Ibrahim Rugova</a> was elected its president in an election in which only Kosovo Albanians participated.<sup id="cite_ref-babuna_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-babuna-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> During its lifetime, the Republic of Kosova was only officially <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">recognised</a> by Albania. By the mid-1990s, the Kosovo Albanian population was growing restless, as the status of Kosovo was not resolved as part of the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Agreement</a> of November 1995, which ended the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>. By 1996, the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Liberation_Army" title="Kosovo Liberation Army">Kosovo Liberation Army</a> (KLA), an ethnic Albanian guerrilla <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary group</a> that sought the separation of Kosovo and the eventual creation of a <a href="/wiki/Greater_Albania" title="Greater Albania">Greater Albania</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> had prevailed over the Rugova's non-violent resistance movement and launched attacks against the Yugoslav Army and Serbian police in Kosovo, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rogel_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogel-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
By 1998, international pressure compelled Yugoslavia to sign a ceasefire and partially withdraw its security forces. Events were to be monitored by <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) observers according to an agreement negotiated by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holbrooke" title="Richard Holbrooke">Richard Holbrooke</a>. The ceasefire did not hold and fighting resumed in December 1998, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Ra%C4%8Dak_massacre" title="Račak massacre">Račak massacre</a>, which attracted further international attention to the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-rogel_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rogel-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Within weeks, a multilateral international conference was convened and by March had prepared a draft agreement known as the <a href="/wiki/Rambouillet_Accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Rambouillet Accords">Rambouillet Accords</a>, calling for the restoration of Kosovo's autonomy and the deployment of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> forces. The Yugoslav delegation found the terms unacceptable and refused to sign the draft. Between 24 March and 10 June 1999, <a href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">NATO intervened</a> by bombing Yugoslavia aimed to force Milošević to withdraw his forces from Kosovo,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> though NATO could not appeal to any particular motion of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Council_of_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Council of the United Nations">Security Council of the United Nations</a> to help legitimise its intervention.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_(Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg/220px-Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg/330px-Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg/440px-Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_%28Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="614" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Missing_Men_of_Krusha_e_Madhe_(Burrat_e_Krushes_se_Madhe).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians" title="Kosovo Albanians">Kosovo-Albanian</a> soldiers holding pictures in memory of the men who were killed or went missing in the <a href="/wiki/Women_of_Krusha_e_Madhe" title="Women of Krusha e Madhe">Massacre of Krusha e Madhe</a></div></div></div><p> Combined with continued skirmishes between Albanian guerrillas and Yugoslav forces the conflict resulted in a further massive displacement of population in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the conflict, roughly a million ethnic Albanians fled or were forcefully driven from Kosovo. In 1999 more than 11,000 deaths were reported to the office of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Carla_Del_Ponte" title="Carla Del Ponte">Carla Del Ponte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kosovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, some 3,000 people were still missing, of which 2,500 are Albanian, 400 Serbs and 100 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> By June, Milošević agreed to a foreign military presence in Kosovo and the withdrawal of his troops. After the Yugoslav Army withdrew, over half of Kosovo's Serbs and other non-Albanians flew or were expelled and many of the remaining civilians were subjected to abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wills_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wills-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, over 90,000 Serbian and other non-Albanian refugees fled the war-torn province. In the days after the Yugoslav Army withdrew, over 80,000 (almost half of 200,000 estimated to live in Kosovo) Serb and other non-Albanians civilians were expelled from Kosovo and many of the remaining civilians were victims of abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wills_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wills-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> After Kosovo and other <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, Serbia became home to the highest number of refugees and <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">IDPs</a> (including Kosovo Serbs) in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In some villages under Albanian control in 1998, militants drove ethnic-Serbs from their homes. Some of those who remained are unaccounted for and are presumed to have been abducted by the KLA and killed. The KLA detained an estimated 85 Serbs during its 19 July 1998 attack on <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">Orahovac</a>. 35 of these were subsequently released but the others remained. On 22 July 1998, the KLA briefly took control of the Belaćevac mine near the town of Obilić. Nine Serb mineworkers were captured that day and they remain on the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a>'s list of the missing and are presumed to have been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In August 1998, 22 Serbian civilians were reportedly killed in the village of Klečka, where the police claimed to have discovered human remains and a kiln used to cremate the bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In September 1998, Serbian police collected 34 bodies of people believed to have been seized and murdered by the KLA, among them some ethnic Albanians, at Lake Radonjić near Glođane (Gllogjan) in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Radonji%C4%87_massacre" title="Lake Radonjić massacre">Lake Radonjić massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_123-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg/220px-Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg/330px-Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg/440px-Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-metohija-koreni-duse029.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Serbian children refugees, Cërnica, Gjilan</div></div></div>
<p>During and after the 1999 war, over three hundred Serb civilians who were taken across the border into Albania were killed in a "Yellow House" near the town of Burrel and had several of their organs removed for sale on the black market. These claims were investigated first by the ICTY who found medical equipment and traces of blood in and around the house.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> They were then investigated by the UN, who received witness reports from many ex-UK fighters who stated that several of the prisoners had their organs removed.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The Chief Prosecutor for the ICTY, Carla Del Ponte, revealed these crimes to the public in her book,<sup id="cite_ref-mmePro_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmePro-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> causing a large response. In 2011, a French media outlet <i>France24</i> released a classified UN document written in 2003 which documented the crimes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia (ICTY) prosecuted crimes committed during the Kosovo War. Nine senior Yugoslav officials, including Milošević, were indicted for <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Crime against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> committed between January and June 1999. Six of the defendants were convicted, one was acquitted, one died before his trial could commence, and one (Milošević) died before his trial could conclude.<sup id="cite_ref-icty_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icty-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Six KLA members were charged with crimes against humanity and war crimes by the ICTY following the war, but only one was convicted.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haradinaj_cleared_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haradinaj_cleared-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war">Post-war</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_status_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo status process">Kosovo status process</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/220px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/330px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg/440px-Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_bondsteel_kosovo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Camp_Bondsteel" title="Camp Bondsteel">Camp Bondsteel</a> is the main base of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> under KFOR command in south-eastern part of Kosovo near the city of <a href="/wiki/Ferizaj" title="Ferizaj">Ferizaj</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On 10 June 1999, the UN Security Council passed <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1244">UN Security Council Resolution 1244</a>, which placed Kosovo under transitional UN administration (UNMIK) and authorised <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> (KFOR), a NATO-led peacekeeping force. Resolution 1244 provided that Kosovo would have autonomy within the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia, and affirmed the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> of Yugoslavia, which has been legally succeeded by the Republic of Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Estimates of the number of Serbs who left when Serbian forces left Kosovo vary from 65,000<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> to 250,000.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Within post-conflict Kosovo Albanian society, calls for retaliation for previous violence done by Serb forces during the war circulated through public culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Herscher14_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herscher14-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Widespread attacks against Serbian cultural sites commenced following the conflict and the return of hundreds of thousands of Kosovo Albanian refugees to their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-Riedlmayer11_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riedlmayer11-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, prolonged negotiations over Kosovo's future status, sociopolitical problems and nationalist sentiments resulted in the <a href="/wiki/2004_unrest_in_Kosovo" title="2004 unrest in Kosovo">Kosovo unrest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RauschBanar246_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RauschBanar246-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Egleder79_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egleder79-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> 11 Albanians and 16 Serbs were killed, 900 people (including peacekeepers) were injured, and several houses, public buildings and churches were damaged or destroyed. 
</p><p>International negotiations began in 2006 to determine the final status of Kosovo, as envisaged under <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1244" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1244">UN Security Council Resolution 1244</a>. The UN-backed talks, led by UN <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_rank" title="Diplomatic rank">Special Envoy</a> <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">Martti Ahtisaari</a>, began in February 2006. Whilst progress was made on technical matters, both parties remained diametrically opposed on the question of status itself.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2007, Ahtisaari delivered a draft status settlement proposal to leaders in Belgrade and Pristina, the basis for a draft <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution">UN Security Council Resolution</a> which proposed 'supervised independence' for the province. A draft resolution, backed by the United States, the United Kingdom and other European members of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Council">Security Council</a>, was presented and rewritten four times to try to accommodate Russian concerns that such a resolution would undermine the principle of state sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russia, which holds a veto in the Security Council as one of five permanent members, had stated that it would not support any resolution which was not acceptable to both Belgrade and Kosovo Albanians.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Whilst most observers had, at the beginning of the talks, anticipated independence as the most likely outcome, others have suggested that a rapid resolution might not be preferable.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After many weeks of discussions at the UN, the United States, United Kingdom and other European members of the Security Council formally 'discarded' a draft resolution backing Ahtisaari's proposal on 20 July 2007, having failed to secure Russian backing. Beginning in August, a "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/troika" class="extiw" title="wikt:troika">Troika</a>" consisting of negotiators from the European Union (<a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Ischinger" title="Wolfgang Ischinger">Wolfgang Ischinger</a>), the United States (<a href="/wiki/Frank_G._Wisner" title="Frank G. Wisner">Frank G. Wisner</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (Alexander Botsan-Kharchenko) launched a new effort to reach a status outcome acceptable to both Belgrade and Pristina. Despite Russian disapproval, the U.S., the United Kingdom, and France appeared likely to recognise Kosovar independence.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> A declaration of independence by Kosovar Albanian leaders was postponed until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_presidential_election,_2008" title="Serbian presidential election, 2008">Serbian presidential elections</a> (4 February 2008). Most <a href="/wiki/Member_State_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member State of the European Union">EU members</a> and the US had feared that a premature declaration could boost support in Serbia for the ultra-nationalist candidate, <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikolić">Tomislav Nikolić</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provisional_self-government">Provisional self-government</span></h3>
<p>In November 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> supervised the first elections for the Kosovo Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> After that election, Kosovo's political parties formed an all-party unity coalition and elected <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Rugova" title="Ibrahim Rugova">Ibrahim Rugova</a> as President and <a href="/wiki/Bajram_Rexhepi" title="Bajram Rexhepi">Bajram Rexhepi</a> (PDK) as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> After Kosovo-wide elections in October 2004, the LDK and AAK formed a new governing coalition that did not include PDK and Ora. This coalition agreement resulted in Ramush Haradinaj (AAK) becoming Prime Minister, while Ibrahim Rugova retained the position of President. PDK and Ora were critical of the coalition agreement and have since frequently accused that government of corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kosovan_parliamentary_election,_2007" title="Kosovan parliamentary election, 2007">Parliamentary elections</a> were held on 17 November 2007. After early results, <a href="/wiki/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i" title="Hashim Thaçi">Hashim Thaçi</a> who was on course to gain 35 per cent of the vote, claimed victory for PDK, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Kosovo" title="Democratic Party of Kosovo">Democratic Party of Kosovo</a>, and stated his intention to declare independence. Thaçi formed a coalition with current President <a href="/wiki/Fatmir_Sejdiu" title="Fatmir Sejdiu">Fatmir Sejdiu</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Democratic_League_of_Kosovo" title="Democratic League of Kosovo">Democratic League</a> which was in second place with 22 percent of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The turnout at the election was particularly low. Most members of the Serb minority refused to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">2008 Kosovo declaration of independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">International recognition of Kosovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2008_unrest_in_Kosovo" title="2008 unrest in Kosovo">2008 unrest in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg/220px-Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg/330px-Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg/440px-Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3467" data-file-height="1916" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Geb%C3%A4ude_der_UNMIK_NEW_BORN_SIGN_PRISTINA_KOSOVO_Giv_Owned_Image_23_August_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Newborn_monument" title="Newborn monument">Newborn monument</a> unveiled at the celebration of the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence proclaimed earlier that day, 17 February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kosovo declared independence from <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> on 17 February 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_proclaim_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_proclaim-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> As of&#32;17&#32;February&#32;2018,&#32;<a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113&#160;UN states</a> recognise its independence, including all of its immediate neighbours, with the exception of Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Since declaring independence, it has become a member of the international institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> though not of the United Nations.
</p><p>The Serb minority of Kosovo, which largely opposes the declaration of independence, has formed the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Serb_Municipalities" title="Community of Serb Municipalities">Community Assembly of Kosovo and Metohija</a> in response. The creation of the assembly was condemned by Kosovo's president Fatmir Sejdiu, while UNMIK has said the assembly is not a serious issue because it will not have an operative role.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
On 8 October 2008, the UN General Assembly resolved, on a proposal by Serbia, to ask the International Court of Justice to render an advisory opinion on the legality of Kosovo's declaration of independence. The advisory opinion, which is not binding over decisions by states to recognise or not recognise Kosovo, was rendered on 22 July 2010, holding that Kosovo's declaration of independence was not in violation either of general principles of international law, which do not prohibit unilateral declarations of independence, nor of specific international law&#160;– in particular UNSCR 1244&#160;– which did not define the final status process nor reserve the outcome to a decision of the Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-icj-cij_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icj-cij-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some rapprochement between the two governments took place on 19 April 2013 as both parties reached the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>, an EU brokered agreement that would allow the Serb minority in Kosovo to have its own police force and court of appeals.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The agreement is yet to be ratified by either parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kosovo" title="Politics of Kosovo">Politics of Kosovo</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kosovo" title="Government of Kosovo">Government of Kosovo</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg/120px-Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg" width="120" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg/180px-Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg/240px-Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i_photo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="250" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i" title="Hashim Thaçi">Hashim Thaçi</a><br /><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Kosovo" title="President of Kosovo">President</a></small></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:96px;max-width:96px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Ramush_Haradinaj_(-125880784).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg/94px-Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg" width="94" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg/141px-Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg/188px-Ramush_Haradinaj_%28-125880784%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="609" data-file-height="773" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Ramush_Haradinaj" title="Ramush Haradinaj">Ramush Haradinaj</a><br /><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kosovo" title="Prime Minister of Kosovo">Prime Minister</a></small></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Kosovo is a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">republic</a>. It is governed by <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a> institutions which derive from the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution</a>, although until the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>, North Kosovo was in practice largely controlled by institutions of Serbia or parallel institutions funded by Serbia. The legislative is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of Kosovo">Parliament</a> and the ministers within their competencies. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kosovo" title="Government of Kosovo">Government</a> exercises the executive power and is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kosovo" title="Prime Minister of Kosovo">Prime Minister</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, the Deputy Prime Ministers and the Ministers of the various ministries.
</p><p>The judiciary is composed of the Supreme Court and subordinate courts, a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Kosovo" title="Constitutional Court of Kosovo">Constitutional Court</a>, and independent prosecutorial institutions. There also exist multiple independent institutions defined by the constitution and law, as well as local governments. It specifies that Kosovo is a "<a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>" and neutral in matters of religious beliefs. Freedom of belief, conscience and religion is guaranteed with religious autonomy ensured and protected. All citizens are equal before the law and <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> is ensured by the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The Constitutional Framework guarantees a minimum of ten seats in the 120-member Assembly for Serbs, and ten for other minorities, and also guarantees Serbs and other minorities places in the Government.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kosovo" title="President of Kosovo">President</a> serves as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and represents the unity of the people, elected every five years, indirectly by the parliament through a <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a> by a two-thirds majority of all deputies. The head of state invested primarily with representative responsibilities and powers. The president has the power to return draft legislation to the parliament for reconsideration and has a role in foreign affairs and certain official appointments.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kosovo" title="Prime Minister of Kosovo">Prime Minister</a> serves as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> elected by the parliament. Ministers are nominated by the Prime Minister, and then confirmed by the parliament. The head of government exercises executive power of the territory.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kosovo" title="Foreign relations of Kosovo">Foreign relations of Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Security_Force" title="Kosovo Security Force">Kosovo Security Force</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_(20303009083).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg/220px-Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg/330px-Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg/440px-Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_%2820303009083%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2102" data-file-height="1202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westbalkankonferenz_Wien_2015_(20303009083).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kosovo participates in the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Process" title="Berlin Process">Berlin Process</a>, a diplomatic initiative linked to the <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">future enlargement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kosovo" title="Foreign relations of Kosovo">foreign relations</a> of Kosovo are conducted through the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Kosovo)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Kosovo)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. As of 2017, 110 out of 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> member states <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">recognise</a> the Republic of Kosovo. Within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union member states">European Union</a>, it is recognised by 23 of 28 members and is a <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Kosovo_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Kosovo to the European Union">potential candidate</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">future enlargement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kosovo is member of several international organizations including the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Road_and_Transport_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="International Road and Transport Union">International Road and Transport Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional_Cooperation_Council" title="Regional Cooperation Council">Regional Cooperation Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe_Development_Bank" title="Council of Europe Development Bank">Council of Europe Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venice_Commission" title="Venice Commission">Venice Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Will_the_EBRD_do_the_right_thing?_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Will_the_EBRD_do_the_right_thing?-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Kosovo's bid to become a member of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> fell three votes short of the two-third majority required to join.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Almost 21 countries maintain <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Kosovo" title="List of diplomatic missions in Kosovo">diplomatic missions</a> in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo maintains 24 <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Kosovo" title="List of diplomatic missions of Kosovo">diplomatic missions</a> and 28 consular missions abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Albania%E2%80%93Kosovo_relations" title="Albania–Kosovo relations">relations with Albania</a> are in a special case, considering that the two share the same language. The <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages of Kosovo">official languages</a> of Kosovo. <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> has an embassy in the capital <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> and Kosovo an embassy in <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a>. In 1992, Albania was the only country whose parliament voted to recognise the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosova" title="Republic of Kosova">Republic of Kosova</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> was also one of the first countries to officially announce its recognition of the Republic of Kosovo in February 2008.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a> 2015 ranked Kosovo 69th out of 163 countries. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kosovo" title="President of Kosovo">President</a> holds the title of commander-in-chief of the military. Citizens over the age of 18 are eligible to serve in the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Security_Force" title="Kosovo Security Force">Kosovo Security Force</a>. Members of the force are protected from discrimination on the basis of gender or ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organisation">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation (NATO)</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> (KFOR) and the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Protection_Corps" title="Kosovo Protection Corps">Kosovo Protection Corps</a> (KPC) in 2008, started preparations for the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Security_Force" title="Kosovo Security Force">Kosovo Security Force</a>. In 2014, the former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kosovo" title="Prime Minister of Kosovo">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Hashim_Tha%C3%A7i" title="Hashim Thaçi">Hashim Thaçi</a> declared, that the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kosovo" title="Government of Kosovo">National Government</a> had decided to establish a Defence Ministry in 2019, officially transform the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Security_Force" title="Kosovo Security Force">Kosovo Security Forces</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Kosovan_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovan Armed Forces">Kosovan Armed Forces</a>, an Army which meets all the standards of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> members with the aim to join the alliance in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Kosovo" title="Law of Kosovo">Law of Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/EULEX" class="mw-redirect" title="EULEX">EULEX</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG/220px-KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG/330px-KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG/440px-KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KP-PK_During_Kosovo_Independence_Parade.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Police" title="Kosovo Police">Kosovan Police</a> (<i>Policia e Kosovës</i>) is the main law enforcement agency in Kosovo.</div></div></div>
<p>The judicial system of Kosovo is a civil law system divided between courts with regular civil and criminal jurisdiction and administrative courts with jurisdiction over litigation between individuals and the public administration. As of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution of Kosovo</a>, the judicial system is composed of the Supreme Court, which is the highest judicial authority, a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Kosovo" title="Constitutional Court of Kosovo">Constitutional Court</a>, and an independent prosecutorial institution. All of them are administered by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Judicial_Council" title="Kosovo Judicial Council">Judicial Council</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Police" title="Kosovo Police">Kosovo Police</a> is the main state law enforcement agency in the nation. After the Independence of Kosovo in 2008, the force became the governmental agency. The agency carries nearly all general police duties such as criminal investigation, patrol activity, traffic policing, border control.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ahtisaari_Plan" title="Ahtisaari Plan">Ahtisaari Plan</a> envisaged two forms of international supervision of Kosovo after its independence such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Civilian_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="International Civilian Office">International Civilian Office</a> (ICO), which would monitor the implementation of the Plan and would have a wide range of veto powers over legislative and executive actions, and the <a href="/wiki/EULEX" class="mw-redirect" title="EULEX">European Union Rule of Law Mission to Kosovo</a> (EULEX), which would have the narrower mission of deploying police and civilian resources with the aim of developing the Kosovo Police and judicial systems but also with its own powers of arrest and prosecution.
The declaration of independence and subsequent Constitution granted these bodies the powers assigned to them by the Ahtisaari Plan. Since the Plan was not voted on by the UN Security Council, the ICO's legal status within Kosovo was dependent on the de facto situation and Kosovo legislation; it was supervised by an <a href="/wiki/International_Steering_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="International Steering Group">International Steering Group</a> (ISG) composed of the main states which recognised Kosovo. It was never recognised by Serbia or other non-recognising states. EULEX was also initially opposed by Serbia, but its mandate and powers were accepted in late 2008 by Serbia and the UN Security Council as operating under the umbrella of the continuing UNMIK mandate, in a status-neutral way, but with its own operational independence. The ICO's existence terminated on 10 September 2012, after the ISG had determined that Kosovo had substantially fulfilled its obligations under the Ahtisaari Plan. EULEX continues its existence under both Kosovo and international law; in 2012 the Kosovo president formally requested a continuation of its mandate until 2014.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minorities">Minorities</span></h3>
<p>The relations between <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians" title="Kosovo Albanians">Kosovo-Albanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Kosovo-Serbs</a> have been hostile since the rise of nationalism in the Balkans during the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._20_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._20-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> During Communism in Yugoslavia, the ethnic Albanians and Serbs were strongly irreconcilable, with sociological studies during the Tito-era indicating that ethnic Albanians and Serbs rarely accepted each other as neighbours or friends and few held interethnic marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Ethnic prejudices, stereotypes and mutual distrust between ethnic Albanians and Serbs have remained common for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The level of intolerance and separation between both communities during the Tito-period was reported by sociologists to be worse than that of Croat and Serb communities in Yugoslavia, which also had tensions but held some closer relations between each other.<sup id="cite_ref-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schabnel,_Albrecht_2001._Pp._24-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite their planned integration into the Kosovar society and their recognition in the Kosovar constitution, the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, Ashkali, and Egyptian communities continue to face many difficulties, such as segregation and discrimination, in housing, education, health, employment and social welfare.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Many camps around Kosovo continue to house thousands of <a href="/wiki/Internally_Displaced_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Internally Displaced People">Internally Displaced People</a>, all of whom are from minority groups and communities.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Because many of the Roma are believed to have sided with the Serbs during the conflict, taking part in the widespread looting and destruction of Albanian property, <a href="/wiki/Minority_Rights_Group_International" title="Minority Rights Group International">Minority Rights Group International</a> report that Romani people encounter hostility by Albanians outside their local areas.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kosovo" title="Districts of Kosovo">Districts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Kosovo" title="Municipalities of Kosovo">Municipalities of Kosovo</a></div>
<p>The Republic of Kosovo is currently divided into seven <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kosovo" title="Districts of Kosovo">districts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <i lang="sq">rajon</i>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr">okrug</span>), according to the Law of Kosovo and the Brussels Agreement of 2013, which stipulated the formation of new municipalities with Serb majority populations. The districts are further subdivided into 38 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Kosovo" title="Municipalities of Kosovo">municipalities</a> (<i><i lang="sq" title="Albanian language text">komunë</i></i>; <i><i lang="sr" title="Serbian language text">opština</i></i>). The largest and most populous district of Kosovo is the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Pristina" title="District of Pristina">District of Pristina</a> with the capital in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, having a surface area of 2,470 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (953.67&#160;sq&#160;mi) and a population of 477,312.
</p>
<table align="center" style="background:none;" cellspacing="3px">

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kosovo" title="Demographics of Kosovo">Demographics of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Kosovo_(1921-2015).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/220px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/330px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png/440px-Population_of_Kosovo_%281921-2015%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1502" data-file-height="846" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Kosovo_(1921-2015).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Population of Kosovo from 1921 to 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the Statistical Office of Kosovo, its population is estimated to be between 1.9 and 2.2 million with the following ethnic composition: 92% <a href="/wiki/Albanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian people">Albanian people</a>, 4% <a href="/wiki/Serb_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Serb people">Serb people</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Bosniak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak people">Bosniak people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gorani_people" title="Gorani people">Gorani people</a>, 1% <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA</a> estimates the following ratio: 88% <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, 8% <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbs of Kosovo">Kosovo Serbs</a> and 4% other ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
According to CIA <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a> estimated data from July 2009, Kosovo's population stands at 1,804,838 persons. It stated that ethnic composition was 88% Albanians, 7% Serbs and 5% of other ethnic groups including Bosniaks, Gorani, Roma, Turks, Ashkalis, Egyptians and <a href="/wiki/Janjevci" title="Janjevci">Janjevci&#160;– Croats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Albanians, steadily increasing in number, have constituted a majority in Kosovo since the 19th century, the earlier ethnic composition being disputed. Kosovo's political boundaries do not quite coincide with the ethnic boundary by which Albanians compose an absolute majority in every municipality; for example, Serbs form a local majority in <a href="/wiki/North_Kosovo" title="North Kosovo">North Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serb_enclaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo Serb enclaves">two other municipalities</a>, while there are large areas with an Albanian majority outside of Kosovo, namely in the neighbouring regions of former Yugoslavia: the north-west of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Pre%C5%A1evo_Valley" title="Preševo Valley">Preševo Valley</a> in Southern Serbia.
</p><p>At 1.3% per year as of 2008 data, ethnic <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in Kosovo">Albanians in Kosovo</a> have the fastest rate of growth in population in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Over an 82-year period (1921–2003) the population of Kosovo grew to 460% of its original size. Whereas Albanians constituted 60% of Kosovo's 500,000 person population in 1931, by 1991 they reached 81% of Kosovo's 2 million person population.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In the second half of the 20th century, Kosovo Albanians had three times higher birth rates than Serbs.<sup id="cite_ref-On_Genetic_Interests:_Family,_Ethnicity,_And_Humanity_in_an_Age_of_Mass_Migration_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-On_Genetic_Interests:_Family,_Ethnicity,_And_Humanity_in_an_Age_of_Mass_Migration-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In addition, most of Kosovo's pre-1999 <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Serb</a> population relocated to Serbia proper following the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> campaign in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Wills_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wills-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Minority_languages_of_Kosovo" title="Minority languages of Kosovo">Minority languages of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Albanian_dialects.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Albanian_dialects.svg/220px-Albanian_dialects.svg.png" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Albanian_dialects.svg/330px-Albanian_dialects.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Albanian_dialects.svg/440px-Albanian_dialects.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Albanian_dialects.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gheg_Albanian" title="Gheg Albanian">Gheg Albanian</a> is widely spoken in Kosovo.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> are the official languages of Kosovo. Almost 95% of the population speaks <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> as their native language, followed by <a href="/wiki/South_Slavic_languages" title="South Slavic languages">South Slavic languages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>. Due to North Kosovo's boycott of the census, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a> resulted in being the second-largest language after Albanian. However, Serbian is de facto the second most spoken language in Kosovo. Since 1999, the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> has become the dominant language in Kosovo, although equal status is given to <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> and special status is given to other <a href="/wiki/Minority_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Minority languages">minority languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Assessing_Minority_Language_Rights_in_Kosovo_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assessing_Minority_Language_Rights_in_Kosovo-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of Kosovo">Parliament</a> adopted the Law on the Use of Languages in 2006 committed Kosovo institutions to ensuring the equal use of Albanian and Serbian as the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, other languages can also gain recognition at municipal level as official languages if the linguistic community represents at least 5% of the total population of municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Law on the Use of Languages</i> gives <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> the status of an official language in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, irrespective of the size of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks of Kosovo">Turkish community</a> living there.<sup id="cite_ref-COE-Municipalities_195-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE-Municipalities-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Although both <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> are official languages, municipal civil servants are only required to speak one of them in a professional setting and, according to Language Commissioner of Kosovo Slaviša Mladenović statement from 2015, no organizations have all of their documents in both languages.<sup id="cite_ref-ECMI-Kosovo_Language_Commissioner_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMI-Kosovo_Language_Commissioner-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Kosovo" title="Municipalities of Kosovo">Municipalities of Kosovo</a> are largely rural, with only eight municipalities having more than 40,000 inhabitants living in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Kosovo" title="List of cities in Kosovo">urban areas</a>.
</p>
