<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kosovo" title="Religion in Kosovo">Religion in Kosovo</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;max-width:282px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg/140px-14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg" width="140" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg/210px-14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg/280px-14_Kisha_Sh%C3%ABn_Palit_%26_Pjetrit_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3615" data-file-height="2594" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Church in <b><a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a></b> <br /> <small>(Kisha Shën Palit dhe Pjetrit)</small></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:136px;max-width:136px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_Prizren,_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG/134px-2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG" width="134" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG/201px-2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG/268px-2011_Prizren%2C_Meczet_Sinana_Paszy_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3297" data-file-height="2472" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Sinan_Pasha_Mosque_(Prizren)" title="Sinan Pasha Mosque (Prizren)">Mosque</a> in <b><a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a></b> <br /> <small>(Xhamia e Sinan Pashës)</small></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>Kosovo is - according to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kosovo" title="Constitution of Kosovo">Constitution of Kosovo</a> - a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> with no official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>. It provides for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and of conscience.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2011 Census, 95.6% of the population of Kosovo were <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kosovo" title="Islam in Kosovo">Muslims</a>. These figures do not represent individual sects operating in Kosovo such as the <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bektashism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bektashism">Bektashism</a>, which are sometimes classified generally under the category of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> 3.69% of the population were Catholic and an equal number or up to 5% Orthodox (the largely Orthodox Serbian minority boycotted the census). The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Kosovo">Catholic</a> Albanian communities are mostly concentrated in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klina" title="Klina">Klina</a>, and in a few villages near <a href="/wiki/Pe%C4%87" title="Peć">Peć</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitina_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitina (town)">Vitina</a>. The Serb minority is largely <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian Orthodox">Serbian Orthodox</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Kosovo" title="Christianity in Kosovo"> Christianity</a> has a long-standing tradition in Kosovo, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">Eastern Roman period</a>. During the Middle Ages, the entire <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan peninsula</a> had been <a href="/wiki/Christianized" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianized">Christianized</a> under both the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>. From 1389 until 1912 Kosovo formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and a high level of <a href="/wiki/Islamization" title="Islamization">Islamization</a> occurred. After  <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> Kosovo was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Secularity" title="Secularity">secular</a> <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> authorities within the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. During that period, the population of Kosovo became increasingly <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularized</a>. As of  2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kosovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> over 90% of its population had <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> backgrounds, most of whom are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> but also including <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Slavs" title="Muslim Slavs">Slavs</a> (who mostly identify themselves as Gorani or Bosniaks) and Turks.
</p><p>According to the 2014 Freedom of Thought reports issued by the <a href="/wiki/International_Humanist_and_Ethical_Union" title="International Humanist and Ethical Union">IHEU</a>, Kosovo ranked first in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and ninth in the world as <i>Free and equal</i> for tolerance towards religion and atheism.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kosovo" title="Economy of Kosovo">Economy of Kosovo</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_Kosovo" title="Industry of Kosovo">Industry of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-lignite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/220px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/330px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kosovo-lignite.jpg/440px-Kosovo-lignite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="467" data-file-height="345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kosovo-lignite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kosovo has the 5th largest <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> reserves in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kosovo" title="Economy of Kosovo">economy</a> of Kosovo is a transition economy. It suffered from the combined results of political upheaval, the following <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav wars</a>, the Serbian dismissal of Kosovo employees and international sanctions on Serbia of which it was then part. Since the independence in 2008, the economy has grown every year. Despite declining foreign assistance, growth of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> averaged over 5% a year. This was despite the <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis_of_2007-08" class="mw-redirect" title="Global financial crisis of 2007-08">global financial crisis of 2009</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> crisis. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Inflation_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Inflation rate">inflation rate</a> has been low. The most economic development, has taken place in the trade, retail and construction sectors. Kosovo is highly dependent on remittances from the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_diaspora" title="Albanian diaspora">Diaspora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">FDI</a> and other capital inflows.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_Country_Report_No_12/100_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_Country_Report_No_12/100-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kosovo's largest trading partners are Albania, Italy, Switzerland, China, Germany and Turkey. The <a href="/wiki/Euro_currency" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro currency">Euro</a> is its official currency.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kosovo" title="Government of Kosovo">Government of Kosovo</a> have signed free-trade agreements with Croatia, Bosnia and Herzegovina, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and the Republic of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buyusa_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buyusa-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo is a <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">Central European Free Trade Agreement (CEFTA)</a> member, agreed with <a href="/wiki/UNMIK" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMIK">UNMIK</a>, and enjoys a free trade within the non-<a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_Kosovo" title="Industry of Kosovo">secondary sector</a> accounted for 22.60 of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> and a general <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a> of 800.000 employees in 2009. There are several reasons for this stagnation, ranging from consecutive occupations, political turmoil and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Kosovo">War in Kosovo</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-gjeografiaa77_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gjeografiaa77-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Electrical_energy_in_Kosovo" title="Electrical energy in Kosovo">electricity sector</a> is considered as one of the sectors with the greatest potential of development.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo has large reserves of lead, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, silver, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, copper, iron and <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Natural_resources_key_to_the_future_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Natural_resources_key_to_the_future-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The nation has the 5th largest lignite reserves in the world and the 3rd in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The Directorate for Mines and Minerals and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimated, that Kosovo had €13.5&#160;billion worth of minerals.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo&#39;s_mineral_resources_at_13.5bn_euros_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo&#39;s_mineral_resources_at_13.5bn_euros-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/220px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/330px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG/440px-Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rahovec_Grapes_and_Wine.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grapes from the <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">Orahovac</a> valley</div></div></div>
<p>The primary sector is based on small to medium-sized family-owned dispersed units.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> 53% of the nation's area is agricultural land and 41% forest and forestry land, whereas 6% for others.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The arable land is mostly used for corn, wheat, pastures, meadows and vineyards. It contributes almost to 35% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> including the forestry sector. <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">Wine</a> has historically been produced in Kosovo. The wine industry is successful and has been growing after <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>. The main heartland of Kosovo's wine industry is in <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">Orahovac</a>, where millions of litres of wine are produced. The main cultivars include <a href="/wiki/Pinot_noir" title="Pinot noir">Pinot noir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merlot" title="Merlot">Merlot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chardonnay" title="Chardonnay">Chardonnay</a>. Kosovo exports wines to Germany and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Kosovo&#39;s_wines_flowing_again_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kosovo&#39;s_wines_flowing_again-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> During the "glory days" of the wine industry, grapes were grown from the vineyard area of 9,000ha, divided into private and public ownership, and spread mainly throughout the south and west of Kosovo. The four state-owned wine production facilities were not as much "wineries" as they were "wine factories". Only the Rahovec facility that held approximately 36% of the total vineyard area had the capacity of around 50 million litres annually. The major share of the wine production was intended for exports. At its peak in 1989, the exports from the Rahovec facility amounted to 40 million litres and were mainly distributed to the German market.<sup id="cite_ref-wine_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wine-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kosovo" title="Tourism in Kosovo">Tourism in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brezovica_run.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/220px-Brezovica_run.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/330px-Brezovica_run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Brezovica_run.jpg/440px-Brezovica_run.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brezovica_run.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brezovica,_Kosovo" title="Brezovica, Kosovo">Brezovica</a> is one of the most visited winter tourist destinations in Kosovo.</div></div></div>
<p>The natural values of Kosovo represents quality tourism resources. The description of Kosovo's potential in tourism is closely related to its geographical location, in the center of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a>. It represents a crossroads which historically dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical times</a>. Kosovo serves as a link in the connection between <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The mountainous west and southeast of Kosovo has great potential for winter tourism. Skiing takes place at the winter resort of <a href="/wiki/Brezovica,_Kosovo" title="Brezovica, Kosovo">Brezovica</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Shar_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Shar Mountains">Shar Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-turizmi_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turizmi-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kosovo is generally rich in various topographical features including high <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a>, steep <a href="/wiki/Rock_formation" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock formation">rock formations</a> and <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">rivers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-turizmi_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turizmi-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brezovica,_Kosovo" title="Brezovica, Kosovo">Brezovica</a>, with the close proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Pristina_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Pristina Airport">Pristina Airport</a> (60&#160;km) and <a href="/wiki/Skopje_%22Alexander_the_Great%22_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Skopje &quot;Alexander the Great&quot; Airport">Skopje Airport</a> (70&#160;km), the resort is a possible destination for international tourists. Other major attractions include the modern capital of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, the historical cities of <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pej%C3%AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Pejë">Peja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gjakova" title="Gjakova">Gjakova</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Ferizaj" title="Ferizaj">Ferizaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gjilan" title="Gjilan">Gjilan</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a> included Kosovo on the list of 41 places to visit in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kosovo" title="Transport in Kosovo">Transport in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/220px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/330px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg/440px-Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3883" data-file-height="2591" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_International_Airport_%22Adem_Jashari%22_Limak_Kosovo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pristina_International_Airport" title="Pristina International Airport">Pristina International Airport</a> (PRN) handles more than 1.7 million passengers per year.</div></div></div>
<p>Currently, there are two main motorways in Kosovo including the <a href="/wiki/Albania%E2%80%93Kosovo_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Albania–Kosovo Highway">R7</a> connecting Kosovo with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/R6_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R6 Motorway (Kosovo)">R6</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> with the Macedonian border at <a href="/wiki/Hani_i_Elezit" class="mw-redirect" title="Hani i Elezit">Hani i Elezit</a>. The construction of the new <a href="/wiki/R7.1_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R7.1 Motorway (Kosovo)">R7.1 Motorway</a> began in 2017.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/R7_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R7 Motorway (Kosovo)">R7 Motorway</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Albania-Kosovo_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Albania-Kosovo Highway">Albania-Kosovo Highway</a>) links Kosovo to <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> coast in <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Durrës</a>. Once the remaining <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">European route (E80)</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> to <a href="/wiki/Merdare" title="Merdare">Merdare</a> section project will be completed, the motorway will link Kosovo through the present <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">European route (E80)</a> highway with the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_corridor_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan-European corridor X">Pan-European corridor X</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E75" title="European route E75">E75</a>) near <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%A1" title="Niš">Niš</a> in Serbia. The <a href="/wiki/R6_Motorway_(Kosovo)" class="mw-redirect" title="R6 Motorway (Kosovo)">R6 Motorway</a> is currently under construction. Forming part of the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E65" title="European route E65">E65</a>, it is the second motorway constructed in the region and it links the capital <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonian</a> border at <a href="/wiki/Elez_Han" title="Elez Han">Elez Han</a>, which is about 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>. Construction of the motorway started in 2014 and it is going to be finished in 2018.
</p><p>The nation hosts two airports, the <a href="/wiki/Gjakova_Airport" title="Gjakova Airport">Gjakova Airport</a> and the only <a href="/wiki/Pristina_International_Airport" title="Pristina International Airport">International Airport of Pristina</a>. The Gjakova Airport was built by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo Force</a> (KFOR) following the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, next to an existing airfield used for agricultural purposes, and was used mainly for military and humanitarian flights. The local and national government plans to offer Gjakova Airport for operation under a public-private partnership with the aim of turning it into a civilian and commercial airport.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pristina_International_Airport" title="Pristina International Airport">Pristina International Airport</a> is located southwest of <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. It is Kosovo's only international airport and the only port of entry for air travelers to Kosovo.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care in Kosovo">Health in Kosovo</a></div>
<p>In the past, Kosovo's capabilities to develop a modern <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> system were limited.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Strategy_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Strategy-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
Low <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> during 1990 worsened the situation even more. However, the establishment of Faculty of Medicine in the <a href="/wiki/Universiteti_i_Prishtin%C3%ABs" title="Universiteti i Prishtinës">University of Pristina</a> marked a significant development in health care. This was also followed by launching different health clinics which enabled better conditions for professional development.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Strategy_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Strategy-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nowadays the situation has changed, and the health care system in Kosovo is organised into three sectors: <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary health care">primary</a>, secondary and tertiary health care.<sup id="cite_ref-Sectorial_Health_Care_Strategy_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sectorial_Health_Care_Strategy-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
Primary health care in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> is organised into thirteen family medicine centres<sup id="cite_ref-prishtina-komuna.org_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prishtina-komuna.org-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> and fifteen ambulantory care units.<sup id="cite_ref-prishtina-komuna.org_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prishtina-komuna.org-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Secondary health care is decentralised in seven regional hospitals. Pristina does not have any regional hospital and instead uses University Clinical Center of Kosovo for health care services. University Clinical Center of Kosovo provides its health care services in twelve clinics,<sup id="cite_ref-Stafi_i_QKUK-se_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stafi_i_QKUK-se-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> where 642 doctors are employed.<sup id="cite_ref-2012_Health_Statistics_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_Health_Statistics-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> At a lower level, home services are provided for several vulnerable groups which are not able to reach health care premises.<sup id="cite_ref-Home_Services_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home_Services-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Kosovo health care services are now focused on patient safety, quality control and assisted health.<sup id="cite_ref-Patient_Safety_and_Quality_Control_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patient_Safety_and_Quality_Control-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kosovo" title="Education in Kosovo">Education in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/220px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/330px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg/440px-Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5942" data-file-height="3967" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo_February_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Kosovo" title="Academy of Sciences and Arts of Kosovo">Academy of Sciences and Arts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>. Honorary members include the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Americans" title="Albanian Americans">Albanian-American</a> Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Ferid_Murad" title="Ferid Murad">Ferid Murad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Albanians in the Republic of Macedonia">Albanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> nun <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Education for primary, secondary, and tertiary levels is predominantly public and supported by the state, run by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Science_and_Technology_(Kosovo)" title="Ministry of Education, Science and Technology (Kosovo)">Ministry of Education</a>. Education takes place in two main stages: primary and secondary education and higher education.
</p><p>The primary and secondary education is subdivided into four stages: preschool education, primary and low secondary education, high secondary education and special education. Preschool education is for children from the ages of one to five. Primary and secondary education is obligatory for everyone. It is provided by gymnasiums and vocational schools and also available in languages of recognized minorities in Kosovo, where classes are held in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, Serbian, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>. The first phase (primary education) includes grades one to five, and the second phase (low secondary education) grades six to nine. The third phase (high secondary education) consists of general education but also professional education, which is focused on different fields. It lasts four years. However, pupils are offered possibilities of applying for higher or university studies. According to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Science_and_Technology_(Kosovo)" title="Ministry of Education, Science and Technology (Kosovo)">Ministry of Education</a>, children who are not able to get a general education are able to get a special education (fifth phase).<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Higher education can be received in universities and other higher-education institutes. These educational institutions offer studies for <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">Master</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> degrees. The students may choose full-time or part-time studies.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kosovo" title="Culture of Kosovo">Culture of Kosovo</a></div>
<p>The cultural traditions of Kosovo has been influenced primarily by the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians" title="Kosovo Albanians">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Serbs" title="Kosovo Serbs">Serbian</a> origins of its majority population. Located geographically at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian people">Albanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic people">Slavic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman people">Ottoman</a> cultures, it has enriched its own culture adopting and maintaining some of the traditions of its neighbours and of other influence sources.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kosovo" title="Sport in Kosovo">Sport in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_(cropped2).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG/170px-Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG" width="170" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG/255px-Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_%28cropped2%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="366" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memli_Krasniqi_meeting_Majlinda_Kelmendi_(cropped2).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Judoka <a href="/wiki/Majlinda_Kelmendi" title="Majlinda Kelmendi">Majlinda Kelmendi</a>, Olympic, World and European Champion.</div></div></div>
<p>Sport is a significant component of the society and culture of Kosovo. The most prominent sports in Kosovo include <a href="/wiki/Football" title="Football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Committee_of_Kosovo" title="Olympic Committee of Kosovo">Olympic Committee of Kosovo</a> became a full member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympic_recognition_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympic_recognition-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> It participated at the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.
</p><p>The most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sport</a> in Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/Football" title="Football">football</a> by far. It was first codified in 1946. In 1922, the first clubs were formed such as the FC Gjakova and <a href="/wiki/FC_Prishtina" title="FC Prishtina">Prishtina</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">cold war</a> era from 1945 until 1991, football in <a href="/wiki/Former_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a> was advancing so fast that in 1946 it was formed the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Kosovo" title="Football Federation of Kosovo">Federation of Kosovo</a>, as a subsidiary of the Federation of Yugoslavia. Prishtina became the most successful club in the <i>First Leagues of Yugoslavia</i>, while <a href="/wiki/KF_Trep%C3%A7a" title="KF Trepça">KF Trepça</a> was part of the league for one year. In 1991, the first independent Federation of Kosovo were founded, after all football players, almost from Kosovo, were banned from the League in Yugoslavia. The first game was held in the stadium of <a href="/wiki/KF_Flamurtari" title="KF Flamurtari">Flamurtari</a> on 13 September 1991 in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, which marked in the same time the start of the first independent championship in Kosovo. The governing body is mainly responsible for <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_national_football_team" title="Kosovo national football team">national team</a> and the most main cup competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Football_in_Kosovo_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Football_in_Kosovo-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bersant_Celina_20160221_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Bersant_Celina_20160221_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2078" data-file-height="2373" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bersant_Celina_20160221_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bersant_Celina" title="Bersant Celina">Bersant Celina</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> to <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian</a> parents and he plays for Welsh club <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Three football players born in Kosovo as <a href="/wiki/Milutin_%C5%A0o%C5%A1ki%C4%87" title="Milutin Šoškić">Milutin Šoškić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fahrudin_Jusufi" title="Fahrudin Jusufi">Fahrudin Jusufi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Durkovi%C4%87" title="Vladimir Durković">Vladimir Durković</a> were part of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia national football team</a>, which won a gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_1960_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a> and a silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/1960_European_Nations%27_Cup" title="1960 European Nations&#39; Cup">1960 European Championship</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Stojanovi%C4%87" title="Stevan Stojanović">Stevan Stojanović</a> from Kosovo, who played for Yugoslavia, was part of <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_Belgrade" title="Red Star Belgrade">Red Star Belgrade</a> and they won <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_European_Cup" title="1990–91 European Cup">1990–91 European Cup</a>.
Nowadays, in many European teams there are players of <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian origin</a> from Kosovo who have had the opportunity to show their talents and values. Thus, <a href="/wiki/Lorik_Cana" title="Lorik Cana">Lorik Cana</a> was the captain of <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Olympique de Marseille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland A.F.C">Sunderland</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Albania_national_football_team" title="Albania national football team">Albania national team</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Valon_Behrami" title="Valon Behrami">Valon Behrami</a> who played for <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, and currently is playing for <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss national football team">Swiss national football team</a>. There are other players who had the opportunity to play for European football teams such as <a href="/wiki/Xherdan_Shaqiri" title="Xherdan Shaqiri">Xherdan Shaqiri</a>, who plays as a midfielder for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland national football team</a><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Januzaj" title="Adnan Januzaj">Adnan Januzaj</a>.
</p><p>Basketball is also one of the favourite sports of the people in Kosovo. The first championship was held in 1991, with the participation of eight teams. The <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Federation_of_Kosovo" title="Basketball Federation of Kosovo">Basketball Federation of Kosovo</a> was accepted as a full member of <a href="/wiki/FIBA" title="FIBA">FIBA</a> on 13 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Notable players born in Kosovo who played for the successful <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia national basketball team">Serbia national teams</a> include Zyfer Avdiu, <a href="/wiki/Marko_Simonovi%C4%87" title="Marko Simonović">Marko Simonović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Musli" title="Dejan Musli">Dejan Musli</a>. Some of them are continued to competing for Serbia after recognition of Kosovo from FIBA.
</p><p>Judoka <a href="/wiki/Majlinda_Kelmendi" title="Majlinda Kelmendi">Majlinda Kelmendi</a> became <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Judo_Championships" title="2013 World Judo Championships">World Champion</a> in 2013 and <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Judo_Championships" title="2014 World Judo Championships">2014</a>, and also the European Champion in <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Judo_Championships" title="2014 European Judo Championships">2014</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics 2016">Summer Olympics 2016</a>, Kelmendi became the first decorated Kosovan athlete to win a gold medal, also the first gold medal for Kosovo in a major sport tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympics_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nora_Gjakova" title="Nora Gjakova">Nora Gjakova</a> won first medal for Kosovo at the <a href="/wiki/European_Games" title="European Games">European Games</a>, when she earned bronze in <a href="/wiki/Judo_at_the_2015_European_Games" title="Judo at the 2015 European Games">57 kg</a> category.
</p>
<div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kosovo" title="Music of Kosovo">Music of Kosovo</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_Ora_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/124px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="124" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/186px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg/248px-Rita_Ora_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1497" data-file-height="1625" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:92px;max-width:92px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Rona_Nishliu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/90px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG" width="90" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/135px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rona_Nishliu.JPG/180px-Rona_Nishliu.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> to <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian</a> parents. (<i>left</i>) <a href="/wiki/Rona_Nishliu" title="Rona Nishliu">Rona Nishliu</a> represented <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Albania_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Albania in the Eurovision Song Contest 2012">2012 Eurovision Song Contest</a> where she finished 5th. (<i>right</i>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/170px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/255px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Lahuta_QKVF.jpg/340px-Lahuta_QKVF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4506" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahuta_QKVF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Lahuta" class="mw-redirect" title="Lahuta">lahuta</a> is used by <a href="/wiki/Gheg_Albanians" class="mw-redirect" title="Gheg Albanians">Gheg Albanians</a> for the singing of epic songs or <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Songs_of_the_Frontier_Warriors" title="Albanian Songs of the Frontier Warriors">Albanian Songs of the Frontier Warriors</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Although the music in Kosovo is diverse, authentic <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Albania" title="Music of Albania">Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian music">Serbian music</a> still exist. <a href="/wiki/Albanian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanian music">Albanian music</a> is characterised by the use of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%87ifteli" title="Çifteli">Çifteli</a>. <a href="/wiki/Classical_music_in_Kosovo" title="Classical music in Kosovo">Classical music</a> is well known in Kosovo and has been taught at several <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-college_music_schools" title="List of pre-college music schools">music schools</a> and universities. In 2014, Kosovo submitted their first film for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Three_Windows_and_a_Hanging" title="Three Windows and a Hanging">Three Windows and a Hanging</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Isa_Qosja" title="Isa Qosja">Isa Qosja</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ThreeWindows_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThreeWindows-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the past, epic poetry in Kosovo and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Albania" title="Northern Albania">Northern Albania</a> was sung on a lahuta and then a more tuneful çiftelia was used which has two strings-one for the melody and one for drone. Kosovan music is influenced by Turkish music due to the almost 500-year span of Ottoman rule in Kosovo though Kosovan folklore has preserved its originality and exemplary.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Archaeological researches tells about how old is this tradition and how was it developed in parallel way with other traditional music in the Balkan. There were found lots of roots since 5th century BC like paintings in the stones of singers with instruments. (Is famous the portrait of "Pani" who was holding an instrument similar to flute)<sup id="cite_ref-Kruta_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kruta-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The contemporary music artists <a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Era_Istrefi" title="Era Istrefi">Era Istrefi</a>, are all of <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian origin</a> and have achieved international recognition for their music.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> One widely recognised musician from <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> is guitarist <a href="/wiki/Petrit_%C3%87eku" title="Petrit Çeku">Petrit Çeku</a>, winner of several international prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Serbian music from Kosovo presents a mixture of traditional music, which is part of the wider Balkan tradition, with its own distinctive sound, and various Western and Turkish influences.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>  Serb songs from Kosovo were an inspiration for 12th song wreath by composer <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Mokranjac" title="Stevan Mokranjac">Stevan Mokranjac</a>. Most of Serbian music from Kosovo was dominated by church music, with its own share of sung epic poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Serbian national instrument <a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">Gusle</a> is also used in Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Viktorija" title="Viktorija">Viktorija</a> is the only artist from Kosovo, who represented <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Yugoslavia in the Eurovision Song Contest">Yugoslavia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Aska_(group)" title="Aska (group)">Aska</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1982" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1982">1982</a>. Singer <a href="/wiki/Rona_Nishliu" title="Rona Nishliu">Rona Nishliu</a> finished 5th in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">2012</a> Eurovision Song Contest, while <a href="/wiki/Lindita_(singer)" title="Lindita (singer)">Lindita</a> represented Albania in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2017" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2017">2017</a>. Several Serbian singers from Kosovo, participates in the Serbian national selection for the Eurovision Song Contest. <a href="/wiki/Nevena_Bo%C5%BEovi%C4%87" title="Nevena Božović">Nevena Božović</a> represented <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Serbia in the Junior Eurovision Song Contest">Serbia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2007" title="Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2007">Junior Eurovision Song Contest</a> and, as member of <a href="/wiki/Moje_3" title="Moje 3">Moje 3</a> in the Eurovision Song Contest.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Kosovo" title="Architecture of Kosovo">Architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Kosovo" title="Monuments of Kosovo">Monuments of Kosovo</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Albanian_heritage_in_Kosovo" title="Destruction of Albanian heritage in Kosovo">Destruction of Albanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Serbian_heritage_in_Kosovo" title="Destruction of Serbian heritage in Kosovo">Serbian heritage in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/220px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/330px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg/440px-Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2742" data-file-height="1823" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prishtina_and_the_great_Hamam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Hamam_of_Pristina" title="Great Hamam of Pristina">Great Hamam of Pristina</a> was built in the 15th century and was part of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Mosque_(Pristina)" title="Imperial Mosque (Pristina)">Imperial Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The architecture of Kosovo dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Age">Middle Ages</a>. It has been influenced by the presence of different civilizations and religions as evidenced by the structures which have survived to this day.
</p><p>Kosovo is home to many <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">Monasteries</a> and Churches from the 13th and 14th century that represents the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a> legacy. Architectural heritage from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Period</a> includes mosques and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">hamams</a> from the 15th, 16th and 17th centuries. Other historical architectural structures of interest include <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Kosovo" title="Monuments of Kosovo">kullas</a> from the 18th and 19th centuries as well as a number of bridges, urban centers and fortresses. While some <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_architecture" title="Vernacular architecture">vernacular buildings</a> are not considered important in their own right, taken together they are of considerable interest. During the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">1999 conflict in Kosovo</a>, many buildings that represent this heritage were destroyed or damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unesco.org_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco.org-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> In the Dukagjini region, at least 500 kullas were attacked, and most of them destroyed or otherwise damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> recognized the <a href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani" title="Visoki Dečani">Visoki Dečani monastery</a> as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> for its outstanding universal value. Two years later, the site of patrimony was extended as a serial nomination, to include three other religious monuments: <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87_(monastery)" title="Patriarchate of Peć (monastery)">Patriarchate of Peć</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Ljevi%C5%A1" title="Our Lady of Ljeviš">Our Lady of Ljeviš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Danica_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Gračanica monastery">Gračanica monastery</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Monuments_in_Kosovo" title="Medieval Monuments in Kosovo">Medieval Monuments in Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> It is consisting of four <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a> churches and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian monasteries">monasteries</a> which represent the fusion of the eastern Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> and the western <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> ecclesiastical architecture to form the Palaiologian Renaissance style. The construction was founded by members of <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a>, the most important dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Serbia in the Middle Ages">Serbia in the Middle Ages</a>.
</p><p>These monuments have come under attack, especially during the <a href="/wiki/2004_unrest_in_Kosovo" title="2004 unrest in Kosovo">2004 ethnic violence</a>. In 2006, the property was inscribed on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_in_Danger" title="List of World Heritage in Danger">List of World Heritage in Danger</a> due to difficulties in its management and conservation stemming from the region's political instability.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:124px;max-width:124px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:101px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Journey_to_the_sky%22,_1977_oil_on_canvas,_107_x_132_cm.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG/122px-%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG" width="122" height="102" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG/183px-%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG/244px-%22Journey_to_the_sky%22%2C_1977_oil_on_canvas%2C_107_x_132_cm.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3011" data-file-height="2508" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:104px;max-width:104px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:101px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Ibrahim_Kodra,_The_date,_1987_oil_on_canvas,_80x100_cm.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG/102px-Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG" width="102" height="102" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG/153px-Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG/204px-Ibrahim_Kodra%2C_The_date%2C_1987_oil_on_canvas%2C_80x100_cm.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2633" data-file-height="2637" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Muslim_Mulliqi" title="Muslim Mulliqi">Muslim Mulliqi</a>, <i>Journey to the sky</i> (1975) <small>(<b>left</b>)</small> <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Kodra" title="Ibrahim Kodra">Ibrahim Kodra</a>, <i>The date</i> (1987) <small>(<b>right</b>)</small></div></div></div>
<p>Kosovan art was unknown to the international public for a very long time, because of the regime, many artists were unable to display their art in art galleries, and so were always on the lookout for alternatives, and even resorted to taking matters into their own hands. During the Kosovo War, many studios were burned down and many artworks were destroyed or lost. Until 1990, artists from Kosovo presented their art in many prestigious worldwide renowned centers. They were affirmed and evaluated highly because of their unique approach to the arts considering the circumstances in which they were created, making them distinguished and original.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Congress2010_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congress2010-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 1979, the <a href="/wiki/Kosova_National_Art_Gallery" title="Kosova National Art Gallery">Kosova National Art Gallery</a> was founded. It became the highest institution of visual arts in Kosovo. It was named after one of the most prominent artists of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Mulliqi" title="Muslim Mulliqi">Muslim Mulliqi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Engj%C3%ABll_Berisha" title="Engjëll Berisha">Engjëll Berisha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masar_Caka" title="Masar Caka">Masar Caka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahir_Emra" title="Tahir Emra">Tahir Emra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_G%C3%ABrguri" title="Abdullah Gërguri">Abdullah Gërguri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hysni_Krasniqi" title="Hysni Krasniqi">Hysni Krasniqi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nimon_Lokaj" title="Nimon Lokaj">Nimon Lokaj</a>, Aziz Nimani, <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_Ramadani" title="Ramadan Ramadani">Ramadan Ramadani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esat_Valla" title="Esat Valla">Esat Valla</a> and Lendita Zeqiraj are some of few <a href="/wiki/List_of_Albanian_painters" title="List of Albanian painters">Albanian painters</a> born in Kosovo.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kosovan_cuisine" title="Kosovan cuisine">Kosovan cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kafe_turke.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Kafe_turke.JPG/220px-Kafe_turke.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Kafe_turke.JPG/330px-Kafe_turke.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Kafe_turke.JPG/440px-Kafe_turke.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kafe_turke.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Turkish coffee is very popular in Kosovo.</div></div></div>
<p>The cuisine in Kosovo is similar to the cuisine of the surrounding places (<a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>), and has been significantly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albanian_cuisine" title="Albanian cuisine">Albanian cuisine</a>. Common dishes include <a href="/wiki/Burek" class="mw-redirect" title="Burek">burek</a>, pies, <a href="/wiki/Flija" class="mw-redirect" title="Flija">flija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sujuk" title="Sujuk">suxhuk</a> and other sausages, <a href="/wiki/Stuffed_peppers" title="Stuffed peppers">stuffed peppers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a>, beans, <a href="/wiki/Sarma_(food)" title="Sarma (food)">sarma</a>, burjan, <a href="/wiki/Pita" title="Pita">pita</a> and rice.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Bread and dairy are important staples in Kosovar Albanian cuisine.
</p><p>The most widely used dairy products are milk, yogurt, <a href="/wiki/Ayran" title="Ayran">ayran</a>, spreads, cheese and <a href="/wiki/Kaymak" title="Kaymak">kaymak</a>. Meat (beef, chicken and lamb), beans, rice and peppers are, likewise, major parts of the Kosovo Albanian diet. Vegetables are used seasonally. Usually, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a> are pickled. Herbs such as salt, black pepper, red pepper and Vegeta are also popular.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditional Kosovan desserts are often made with sherbet, which is cooked sugar with either lemon or vanilla flavor. <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">Baklava</a> is one of the most widely used pastries in Kosovo. Another is Kajmaçin, which is composed of baked eggs, mixed with sugar and oil. Sheqer Pare is a pastry similar to baklava, as it is topped with sherbet.
</p><p>Other pastries such as <a href="/wiki/Ka%C4%8Damak" title="Kačamak">Kaqamak</a>, Tespishte, Rovani, <a href="/wiki/Tulumba" title="Tulumba">Tulluma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%AApe" title="Crêpe">Pallaqinka</a> are also a very popular breakfast foods in Kosovo. They are usually topped with Nutella, cheese, or honey. Shampite or <a href="/wiki/Lokum" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokum">Llokuma</a> is served as a treat for children, and mostly as the first treat to guests on the days of <a href="/wiki/Eid_al_Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid al Fitr">Bajram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Kosovo" title="Cinema of Kosovo">Cinema of Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kino-Kalaja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/220px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/330px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Kino-Kalaja.jpg/440px-Kino-Kalaja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kino-Kalaja.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dokufest" title="Dokufest">Dokufest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a>. <br /> <i>"Kosovo is known more for conflict than culture, but at a film festival in the country’s prettiest town, partying and arts mix to great effect."</i> – <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guardian (newspaper)">The Guardian</a><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> </div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/170px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/255px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg/340px-Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1109" data-file-height="1518" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odissea_Bekim_Fehmiu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bekim_Fehmiu" title="Bekim Fehmiu">Bekim Fehmiu</a> was the first Eastern European actor to star in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> during the Cold War.</div></div></div>
<p>The film industry of Kosovo dates from the 1970s. In 1969, the parliament of Kosovo established <i>Kosovafilm</i>, a state institution for the production, distribution and showing of films. Its initial director was the actor Abdurrahman Shala, followed by writer and noted poet Azem Shkreli, under whose direction the most successful films were produced. Subsequent directors of Kosovafilm were Xhevar Qorraj, Ekrem Kryeziu and Gani Mehmetaj. After producing seventeen feature films, numerous short films and documentaries, the institution was taken over by the Serbian authorities in 1990 and dissolved. Kosovafilm was reestablished after <a href="/wiki/FR_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="FR Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> withdrawal from the region in June 1999 and has since been endeavoring to revive the film industry in Kosovo.
</p><p>The International <a href="/wiki/Dokufest" title="Dokufest">Documentary and Short Film Festival</a> is the largest film event in Kosovo. The Festival is organized in August in <a href="/wiki/Prizren" title="Prizren">Prizren</a> which attracts numerous international and regional artists. In this annually organized festival films are screened twice a day in three open air cinemas as well as in two regular cinemas. Except for its films, the festival is also well known for lively nights after the screening. Various events happen within the scope of the festival: workshops, DokuPhoto exhibitions, festival camping, concerts, which altogether turn the city into a charming place to be. In 2010 Dokufest was voted as one of the 25 best international documentary festivals.In 2010 Dokufest was voted as one of the 25 best international documentary festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>International actors of <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Albanians in kosovo">Albanian origin</a> from Kosovo include <a href="/wiki/Arta_Dobroshi" title="Arta Dobroshi">Arta Dobroshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Biberi" title="James Biberi">James Biberi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faruk_Begolli" title="Faruk Begolli">Faruk Begolli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bekim_Fehmiu" title="Bekim Fehmiu">Bekim Fehmiu</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Prishtina_International_Film_Festival" title="Prishtina International Film Festival">Prishtina International Film Festival</a> is the largest film festival, held annually in Pristina, in Kosovo that screens prominent international cinema productions in the Balkan region and beyond, and draws attention to the Kosovar film industry.
</p><p>The movie <a href="/wiki/Shok_(film)" title="Shok (film)">Shok</a> was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Live_Action_Short_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Live Action Short Film">Academy Award for Best Live Action Short Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">88th Academy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The movie was written and directed by Oscar nominated director <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Donoughue" title="Jamie Donoughue">Jamie Donoughue</a>, based on true events during the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosovo war">Kosovo war</a>. Shok's distributor is Ouat Media, and the social media campaign is led by <a href="/wiki/Team_Albanians" title="Team Albanians">Team Albanians</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kosovo" title="Media of Kosovo">Media of Kosovo</a></div>
<p>Kosovo ranked 58th in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> report compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, while in 2016, it ranked 90th.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg/170px-Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg/255px-Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg 2x" data-file-width="333" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aferdita_Dreshaj.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Af%C3%ABrdita_Dreshaj" title="Afërdita Dreshaj">Afërdita Dreshaj</a> was crowned <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_Kosovo" title="Miss Universe Kosovo">Miss Universe Kosovo</a> in 2011.</div></div></div><p>The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kosovo" title="Media of Kosovo">Media</a> consists of different kinds of communicative media such as radio, television, newspapers, and internet web sites. Most of the media survive from advertising and subscriptions. As according to IREX there are 92 radio stations and 22 television stations.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> is an important fashion design, production and trade hub in the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian-speaking</a> territories. Kosovo has been well documented for its success in global beauty pageantry at <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe" title="Miss Universe">Miss Universe</a>. Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Miss_Kosovo" title="Miss Kosovo">Miss Kosovo</a> is a closely followed event throughout the Kosovo. The first titleholder was <a href="/wiki/Zana_Krasniqi" title="Zana Krasniqi">Zana Krasniqi</a>, who placed as a <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2008#Results" title="Miss Universe 2008">Top 10</a> finalist at the <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2008" title="Miss Universe 2008">2008 Miss Universe</a> pageant. She is the first ever <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kosovo" title="Demographics of Kosovo">Kosovo-Albanian</a> woman to enter and place in the contest finishing 6th, just two tenths of a point from the top five. The following year turned out to be another success for the <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_Kosovo" title="Miss Universe Kosovo">Miss Universe Kosovo</a> pageant: <a href="/wiki/Marigona_Dragusha" title="Marigona Dragusha">Marigona Dragusha</a> placed <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2009#Results" title="Miss Universe 2009">second runner-up</a> to <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2009" title="Miss Universe 2009">Miss Universe 2009</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> making her to be the first delegate from Kosovo to make it top the top five.
</p><p>In terms of placements, <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_Kosovo" title="Miss Universe Kosovo">Kosovo</a> has been one of the most successful entrants into the <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe" title="Miss Universe">Miss Universe</a> pageant. Ever since debuting in 2008, Kosovo has missed the semi-finals only twice, in 2010 and 2014, beating many countries that have been competing for decades.
</p><p>Katarina Šulkić from <a href="/wiki/Zve%C4%8Dan" title="Zvečan">Zvečan</a> became 2015 <a href="/wiki/Miss_Serbia" title="Miss Serbia">Miss Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/An%C4%91elka_Toma%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Anđelka Tomašević">Anđelka Tomašević</a> from <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Potok" title="Zubin Potok">Zubin Potok</a> represented Serbia at the <a href="/wiki/Miss_Earth_2013" title="Miss Earth 2013">Miss Earth 2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2014" title="Miss Universe 2014">Miss Universe 2014</a>.
</p>

</div></td></tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3"><div><sup><small>1</small></sup> <span class="wrap"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Kosovo</a> is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008, but <a href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia&#39;s reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo has received formal recognition as an independent state from <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> out of 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>.</span></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
